de la routure dou ventre	of the evacuation of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur;	When other routes come into other parts and are known, and you see that they do not grow further, then you make the cautery of the cautery retreat in proportion to their quantity, and either take a third of the dose;
aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit;	after the cure according to what we have said.</start_of_turn>
et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	and none of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with the cautery at three angles according to this form.</start_of_turn>
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the limb of the shoulder and make a line perpendicular to the breadth below the wound, and another at a distance, and hold your hand firmly against the entire burn with the clamp of the burn
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first burns are lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in no limb.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, or in the shoulder or in the wound, and this pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment does not suffice, then it is necessary to burn it with the burn which is called "points", and the burn must be made according to the length of the limb and the size and weakness and virtue and location of the swelling and the pain
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien;	If he is sane after the first cautery, that is well;
se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sane after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the cautery on that [area], for it is customary that it must move to the adjacent limb, because it is certain that you will make the cauteries until the patient is sane.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, or from sitting or injury, and the pain persists, and medical treatment is of no avail, then it is expedient that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points," or with other cauteries according to the length of the limb, its smallness and its weakness and its virtue and its location of torsion and its pain. If it is healed after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure once more, for it is customary to burn the surrounding area until the patient is healed.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease never helps itself with a cautery, and the same ailment that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief:	Can you see the cautery being done? Take care if the illness is at its beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and do not linger, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the illness, then make five cauteries on the head:
I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous;	I hold the head new, and the other toward the front at the end of the beard;
et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel;	And upon the two horns, and one behind the heel.
et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir;	And I leave the hand as long as the cautery approaches the bone, and as long as the humors escape through the pores so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape from it.
et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The cautery is performed on the mouse according to what is before it
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse;	And if the mixture is everywhere sparse;
et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules;	and it appears clearly, so I command you to cauterize from those which we have said or before, and I cauterize under the neck, two on the shoulder blades, six on the spine of the back, one on the buttock and another behind, two on the two elbows
et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains;	And upon the shoulders, and upon the tendons down below, and one upon every joint of the hands and feet, and upon the ditches of the hands.
et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler;	And beware of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, do not burn them.
et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And never make the cautery upon the heel bone, or upon the rib bone, or upon the liver
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite;	And the more you do the cautery, the more you help, and the more useful it is to him
et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the patients do not feel any pain from the cautery if it is done properly, because the body is already corrupted
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it must be known that the cautery should be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you observe in the handling of things.</start_of_turn>
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, leave the wound covered with flour for some time with honey and other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre;	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not serious, then you must make cautery upon the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb;
et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur;	Or let the cautery be applied once in the middle of the expanse of the burn;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then hold the burn until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure;	And never do we burn on hand, foot, or back, at the issue of nerves that cause the limb to move, and thus if it is bone, it swells
et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	and do not do anything else that does not know the limbs and the issues of nerves moving bone
de albaras	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is ordered to perform cautery on the limb according to the extent and degree of the swelling; and let the cautery penetrate deep into the flesh as much as possible. Then treat the wound until it is healed. And under no circumstances shall cautery be performed on the hand, foot, or back, at the risk of damaging the nerve that moves the limb, or if the swelling is bony. And in all cases, do not interfere with the swelling unless you are familiar with the limb and the course of its moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color;	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the remedies of medicine are of no avail, then burn with a cautery once in the middle of the expanse of the burn, according to the quantity of the burn, until the burn is bony and its color is changed
puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie;	Then sometimes the cure of oatmeal with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of almond, each part in equal measure.
et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And sometimes mix them all together, and bind them with a bandage, and keep them warm until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, if you cauterize with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre;	And thus they say that we must also cauterize the middle of the abscess.</start_of_turn>
et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois;	And I do not believe that this is good, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times.</start_of_turn
et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And it is better to cauterize around the circumference, at the cautery which is called "circle," as we have said previously.</start_of_turn
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens;	When anyone has an ailment which is called "adubelati", and it lingers in meandering or by the excessive abundance which it causes or by the swelling of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and there is little blood remaining, or by the tension;
et tu la vues haster de meurer:	and you must see it hasten to its end.
adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant;	therefore cauterize around the mouth of little cauteries by pricking;
aprés le laisse ensi.	leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to recover.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see her perish with all the cautery, if she is burning too much, make the cautery less: for this is its form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this ailment that is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have perceived the pain, and be such cauteries that the patient feels relief in parts as the disease progresses
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then leave it until it is perfectly healed
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another symptom of disease which is called "corrodens" is nothing other than a weakening of the limbs, because it makes them soft like dry bones.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est;	If you see this ailment in which there is suffering from fire cautery altogether, then cover the large and small cauteries closely, according to what is suitable for the limb or the ailment is
aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	therefore cauterize all the parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and that nothing remains of it except bone
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs a broth of oil until the blisters caused by the fire are ossified, and all the corruption is gone
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the treatment of these wounds with oil, there remains char.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin;	And if after three days the hair does not grow, it is well.
et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If not, repeat the cautery on what remains corrupted from the root
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu;	And this swelling never heals with water medicine rather than fire cautery
mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division:	but indeed fire cautery is of greater aid, as I have already said in the division
pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Take what you need of it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it happens that when a piece has fallen out of place, a disease arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great thing that causes the limb to swell up
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges;	Fire cautery is like a needle of felt; make it of good iron of the size that it can penetrate the root of all parts, and that there are subtle margins;
aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou;	After putting all the clothes on top of the limb, and bending your hand all the way into the limb until it reaches the front of the limb;
et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture;	and leave it [the hand] there for three days until it starts to smell of decay.
puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Then make a dressing of coarse rue leaves bruised with oil, and leave the dressing on all night, and bind firmly and it will be extracted from its root
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of swelling by raising it as high as possible until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude;	And if they turn yellow by discharges of pus, and often happen in the hands and feet, if you must, bring a hot cautery.
et est en teil maniere:	it is partly like this:
pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues;	take a flax cord or iron rod, or a needle of gutta, and put it on the limb and the nail, that is to say over the nails;
et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine;	And put the bandage upon so that it embraces all around, then put a little of warm oil, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand back as the margin of the bandage comes to the root of the nail, and you will find the warm water way deep up to the root.
et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre;	And give the patient a little the biting of the warm water for an hour.
puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	Then leave him like that, and it will discharge all at its roots
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	In this way do another after another, until you have scraped away all that is on the bone, then cure the wounds which cause swelling.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee;	When there is tremor of cold from nerves, or from quartan fever or from some other, if you must do it, make three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one between the shoulder blades
et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire;	and one on the stomach at the olive cautery
si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	If he leaves it trembling, and hastens the patient's sanity from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	When anyone trembles from cold, or from a quartan fever, or from any other cause, if you shall make for him three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery on the flank and one on the stomach at the olive cautery, he will recover from the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Blood sometimes appears through discharge, or abscesses filled with pus, which come from corrupt matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule:	When you see that it is necessary, as soon as you do, that you perform cautery upon each head of the pustule.
un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	A subtle cautery of mustard seed, from which the point may be grasped by fire, or of angelica root long, or by the lentibular cautery
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez;	And never should you cauterize at the beginning when you see it, according to this method, but it should be broken by the excess from which it comes, and you will be healed;
mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is severed.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses;	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things;
et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	It is a grievous thing to extend it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus;	And whenever this happens without any reason, if you hasten to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and strain it too much without calming it down, there will be no more bleeding;
puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge;	Then apply the olive cautery to the wound several times, small and large, until they are all red
puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Then I touch it, great or small according to the wound and the location where the artery is blocked, and put the cautery on this vein while holding your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is necessary.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts suddenly when you remove your thumb from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold of the cautery immediately.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez;	Do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding is stopped
et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide;	Leave the beard that is below untouched, and let no other harm come upon the patient.
et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit:	And keep the beard that is below undisturbed, and let no other evil remain upon the patient; for when the artery is large, we cannot adequately restore it by ourselves, except in three ways as we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc;	Or by cautery, or by extraction if it is not otherwise treated, or by strong stitching with thread, or by medicines placed upon it which have power to restore blood flow.</start_of_turn
et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And be bound and strained immediately.</start_of_turn>
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings about the restoration of the limb with great care of cloths or of placing things burning upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit, it is to no avail.</start_of_turn>
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne;	And if this happens to him and there is neither remedy nor medicine available, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and hold it firmly until it is healed from under the wound and from under the vein.</start_of_turn
et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez;	Do not move it [the shoulder], but moisten it with cold water often so that it becomes cold as much as possible until it is frozen and engrossed and rests.
et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Make incisions in front of those where it has to be cauterized and medicated.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encourag le second livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres;	We have already said in the previous chapter that all diseases in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or apply warming medicine should be treated with cautery of fire or burning medicine, and that we should remove the causes, signs, symptoms, and forms of the cautery
et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	I have added this chapter about the head of the shoulder, and I will return to this chapter by the same way as before for what we have found to be lighter in this matter
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, it is necessary to say, my friend, that there is more danger and fear in this chapter concerning the cautery than in all the others, and for this reason it requires greater caution.</start_of_turn>
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses;	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	Where there is doubt and fear, and comes the death of many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you must not act rashly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many people come to grief through reckless actions.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice;	When such things happen, it is because of their ailment which causes them to move carelessly, and from the greatness of their pain and sickness.
et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Therefore we must have fear of these things.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit:	And of these things one must ask meaning, and it is said:
«atendez, je sui garis»;	Wait, I am finished.
et li maladie est despitouse.	and the sickness is fierce.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los;	I can only advise you to give your best to those things which come from these people who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not do anything rashly but thoughtfully of what you are certain, and of what you have learned and known
et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie;	And use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health is either preserved or converted.
et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	and this will help you to achieve renown, glory, and lasting memory
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Sirs, you must understand and approve of what I say, and if the Holy Inspiration of his hand stirs you up, amen.</start_of_turn>
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I vos ai ordonné cet chapitre en divisant par Chapitre, selon que ce qui est devant ou Chapitre des cauteries, que j’avais devisé des le chef jusque piez, pour ce qui que vous trouvez plus légèrement ce qui vous a été nécessaire.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, which I have divided from the head to the toes, for which you will find it lighter what you have needed
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant;	The disease often causes the swelling of the belly of children, and when the swelling is too great, the head of the child is bent forward
et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	and never is this caused by any response that has been omitted
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors;	I have never seen this disease except in the belly of a woman who is in labor; and all those whom I have seen with it have died suddenly
et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	and therefore I think it is better for me to leave the work in parts for the treatment of diseases
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir;	And I saw one child whose shoulder was completely swollen with fluid, and the head of the shoulder was swelling so much that he could not bear it.
et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os;	and the moisture had become so thick that it was like blood, and this moisture is collected between the bones above the socket, between the head and the bone;
et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large;	and if the moisture is between the head and the bone, and the abscess is small, you must make a wide incision at the head of the shoulder
et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre;	and as long as the moisture is corrected
et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	once the limb has its proper shape again:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater and the incision is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut:	and if the moisture is from the bone, and if you see the edges of the head of the shoulder drawn outwards, and there is pain when you press your hand into it, and this does not go away:
si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If it seems that you have to make three incisions around the head of the shoulder in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out the moisture thoroughly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor;	If it seems that you have to make three incisions around the head of the shoulder in this manner: after that, restrain the incisions of the cloth and the powder, put in wine and oil, and leave for five days.
puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then take it off, and heal the wound with stitches and ointments, and leave the shoulder immobilized, and feed the patient dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue;	And another method of incision is that you look at or open the apex of the abscess, and gather the pus;
car aucune fois est elle devant;	for it is never before
aucune fois derrier;	it is never behind.
aucune fois en destre;	Nevermore in distress;
et aucune fois en senestre.	Nevermore in distress; and nevermore in weakness.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir;	Therefore, when you open the wound or the abscess, and the liquid flows out according to its desire; do what you must and as you desire it
et warde que tu ne coper l’artere;	Beware that you do not cover the artery;
et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	And the vein flows blood, so that the patient dies from excess blood and the evacuation of moisture
de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the filling of the liquid, and you do as you please; but beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, for if the patient dies from excessive bleeding and evacuation of moisture.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease that is called a "catarre," there are blisters or swellings, and the disease is ancient, and the cure of medicine does not help much, then the only cure is to cauterize with that which we can cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief;	You must therefore see that the patient raises his head;
aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel;	after you have rubbed the limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open, then gently move the patient’s head backwards towards the drape;
puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues;	Then look or the vein breaks, and the blood of one and the other is behind the ears, and then they are restored.
puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then signs of the blood clot are seen, then grasp one and the other with a sharp spatula two parts, until the size of the vein reaches the bone, and that is from the root of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see, grasp the sponge from the artery and hold it below, cutting as much as .ij. should through the hole.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, if you do not hold it tightly above continuously, the blood will spurt out.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os;	And if the artery does not open to the touch, if you think, measure the quantity of the space of three fingers, then sign of blood clot and make it reach the bone;
et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere;	and what is to be done with the blood put out if it is six fingers, and by chance more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the refilling of the artery;
puis regarde la plaie:	Then look at the wound:
s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point downwards, if the cord that supports it is severed, then strain the wound and hold it tight, and cure it until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on sensing, if you must measure the quantity of the space of two fingers' breadth, then mark with ink and stop just at the bone; and whatever is above that must be considered blood, for it is worth five and a half coins, or sometimes more or less, according to what the patient can suffer and the filling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if it remains on the point of the spur, if the ribs that support the wound do not suffice, then strain the wound and tie it up, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient dropsy comes, and acute catarrh, because of the tears and the choleric humours in the temples and the ancient sode, which are forsened and remain like other things, and it is treated by means of medicinal cures and all that does not profit, except for the evacuation of the temples' arteries and their cautery, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit;	And the method of extracting them is that if the patient frequently pulls out his hair from his temples, and understands the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well with its beating, and is not returned with great force as in some foolish people who are too cold;
et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement;	and if it is returned, then strain the patient’s neck with some bandages, then wipe the limb of any rough scab, and bathe the limb with warm water until the artery opens clearly
puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Then take the pliers and this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie;	Then take the pliers and slightly stretch the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it up and you will see holes, and withdraw well from the threads that are underneath the navel part.
et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	And if the artery is fragile, if the vein has a point at the armpit, then cut that part according to the quantity of blood
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not secured, if you do not hold it tight without doubt in all things.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III;	And pull out blood six times, up to three times
et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc;	And if the artery is large, if you can tie it in two loops with a strong silk thread, that putrefaction does not appear before the healing of the wound, and evacuate blood slowly
puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez;	Then cut off the excess that is between the two lines in that hour, and then, if you see it, if you cauterize with a fine cautery iron until the blood is stopped;
et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And this is the idleness of the patient, when the patient has no fever and is of a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors:	For the cautery is useful for finishing off moisture.
por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	because it is more helpful for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites;	Or it is useful for extracting veins that are filled with much cotton and put on well-made bandages.

And what is more delicate and lighter in the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery penetrating from two parts, but the penetrating must be well thick in order to hold it longer warm.

des larmes	And must have between the joints a space of one finger’s breadth. et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	If the fracture is great, if you join it with a bandage, and cure it until it is healed;
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not use force, for it will straighten out by itself and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	If the large intestine has descended into the ear towards the upper part, reverse the bowel, grasp the large intestine with one hand, and pull it out with the other hand; press from one side and the other
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	And if the marrow is loosened by the incision, it matters not.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And when the marrow is cut, if you let out the dirty oil, it will heal the limb of that which is causing pain as long as the patient is well.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the blood
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	The wax is a fat enclosed in paper tissues, and this happens more with the people of noble birth, and it causes their eyes to become dry, and they come to have a discharge in the mornings, and they cannot bear the light of the sun because of this.</start_of_turn>
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	And because of this, they lie with their faces downwards, and sleep on them, and their paper tissues are soaked with moisture, and they swell and appear to be covered in wax which bursts in the oil.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand to your chest and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And thus, if the patient places his head in his stomach;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	then take a drape of linen and make an opening in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains the excess of flesh from the chest part, and put it on him.>
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press from both sides, so that the excess is gathered in the circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	then insert moisture in the middle of the tough membrane cutting a wide opening, and do not make it any larger than the wound made to the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	and make the skin taut as long as you see the excess.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	and in various situations, there comes out excess from the opening, according to the shape of a piece of white fat
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract the thumb entirely from a thick piece of charcoal between your thumbs, and twist your hand to the right and to the left until it is scattered.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And keep that you do not touch the edges, that you do not live on the whole expanse until the fat has rendered, that you do not burn it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if it comes out does not open at the beginning of the incision, if you enlarge the incision slightly until it opens.</start_of_turn
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then pull it out as we have said, then moisten the bandage with oil and water, and put on the limb, and strain the bend.</start_of_turn>
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who break their nails and put it on to cover up this moisture that remains
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the cure as long as it is sound
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the vein being cut above, if the treatment of closing wounds is applied as soon as it is sane.
des poilz des papieres	of hair papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When paper nails grow long, do not pluck them out except as nature dictates, and they will become stiff; if they are plucked out, the eyes will be damaged, and will bring about weeping, like tears which are accustomed to cause swelling and softening of the paper and mucus, as much as it causes the destruction of the eyes.</start_of_turn
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And it is the cure in three ways:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	Or by complete fire cautery, or by water medicine as it is before or alongside the fire cautery, and is made by incision and suture or by sutures, as I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the patient’s limb in your left hand, then turn the limb of the oil towards your left hand;
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is converted, it is good;
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	if not, if there is a hook at all its thread underneath
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	then either pull out the margin of the limb or the hairs are born without these hairs, and draw the thread underneath the limb, and turn the limb over
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	Then do in the lower part the papier, the hairs at the joints, on all the circumference, from the great lip to the little;
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	Then take out the thread and put on the paper a little attempt of cotton and bandage, then mark on the paper a sign like a nail, as if like the head of a nail, and know that the sign must be in proportion to the quantity that you see elevate the paper which is intended for you.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if in any part that has been treated there is a great quantity of the paper according to that which the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	Then do on all the circumference up to two lines that you have marked, from the great lip to the little;
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	And if it is one of the cuts near the hair roots in the thickness of a root, then bind it up in one of the two angles of the knee, and then scald it all.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	Then join the two limbs with a staple of a needle with all the fine thread, and wipe away the blood, and make air the excess of thread above the two sockets until you see it done; otherwise.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if this does not suffice, if there is no remedy, then leave the staple and the thread for three days or four; otherwise.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	then treat the wound with drying and constricting things, because the moisture reappears at the bottom of the wound and the reunion of the limb, but the staple is dry (as they say the old ones), and this is work in vain;
et si a une autre maniere:	And if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: if you mark the mark of a figure that is as wide as the head of a berry, as we have told, at three finger-widths distant according to the shape that is here shown.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then hold back what is above with small forces equally according to the shape which is like this
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you are unable to hold the pliers, and the thing is not going right, take a needle or there are a few threads, and grasp the mark with them
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	and bind the other thread tightly with great pressure, and the second thread tightly with little pressure, and assemble between your two the threads equally
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then keep your hand equally, and keep all the skin around where you have marked it, as we have told, and then assemble the two layers of the wound with sutures, and cure until it is healed
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	If the incision comes up to the abscess, apply a cerate and some soft and soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and never is it that the hair of the papilla is converted
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if you do as we have said concerning the incision;
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the costure in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment for wounds is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and that you convert the hair and fat according to what I have said, and then make two incisions by art, and two sutures as long as the hair and as wide as a thumb;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and hold as two cuts of two parts or you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	Then assemble the one and the other together securely over that which is immersed in the marrow of the oil, and strain the two thumbs of the two parts forward.
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	And leave it [the thumb] in place for a while, and the skin which is strained will be torn away and necrosed and will swell, so that it will hurt by itself.</start_of_turn>
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it is late, if the bone has force, then cure it until it is healed.</start_of_turn
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound is closed and the marrow is raised, and the hair will no longer prick.</start_of_turn
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the form of the two thumbs which you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.</start_of_turn
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is one thread of silk that is subtle and flexible.
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then assemble the bones and hold them together subtly, and let the length of the thread be equal to the breadth of a palm
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk beforehand, and do not tie the knots of the thread;
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the patient's hand in its proper position;
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	and if the work is delicate, so that the work is seen to be faded, for it is a subtle and small work, then take hold of the needle at the root of the hair and make it penetrate deeply until you see it emerge from its natural place
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then draw out the hair until above the chase, and keep the chase until there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then draw out your hand as long as the hair veins outwards to the tip of the chase in the palm with the natural hair growth
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chase is treated and the hair does not prick with it, if you draw the chase to the end as you have ordered, until the chase vein appears through and you see it by the vision of the oil;
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then draw the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair returns to its place and the wound heals atop;
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hair is little, if accompany one long hair of the natural kind, and either remove it with that or leave it, as long as it is elongated and then let it go.
de la porriture de l’oil	From the putrefaction of the oil.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the inflammation comes to the head, if there are two methods:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment which is called "aleacrati" or the inflammation comes to the head, if there are two methods: the one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there follows by consequence of wound, or of burn or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of working in it is that you make that suture there, dry the wounds, put in lint wads, and keep it until it is healed
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	and do not use anything but dry and restrictive things in the treatment of it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before;
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but give soft things, such as fennel.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the rose of the aquilegia or altea and linseed seeds be boiled, and aquilon oil melted in none of the oils, and it covers a cloth, and the patient is cured of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasure of your cure is that you must guard it so that it does not harden like before;
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	These works that we have mentioned are not for other purposes than for this disease, that they do not return like before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the cauldron which comes in the oil.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is often called "axacrati", is natural and sudden.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	The accidents come from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the way of the work in this case is that if you take an awl, because it has two threads, and the thread is in the flesh, and it makes the liquid blood come out as much as it wants, so that the thread of the vein breaks in two pieces of the flesh.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then is the cauldron upon the fire with all the needles, and the bowl has a wide lip.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the sponge returns to its place as it should, that is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take the forceps and put them into the sponge, and tear the sponge, and make two incisions through the sponge; or cut through the sponge itself
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	And make two incisions at the two angles of the incision that you made, and make one angle so that when they are put together, the figure is as if it were the letter that has not “two knees.”
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	Then break the cauldron, according to the quantity of bones that are left and those that are detached, of that which surrounds the sponge, and then join the two separated parts with a thread of linen;
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then comes the treatment of what we have said of soft medicines and bandages, as long as it is sane.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the disease comes from a wound or swelling or cautery, if you must make a full incision to remove the hair from the paper, and do as it is above mentioned.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	Then take away between two fingers of a bandage, as I have said before.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and you must make the work according to the form of the disease, for it is diverse in form, and the physicians know best how to make it return to its natural shape
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the patient himself, according to what is convenient in various situations
dou soudement de la papiere	If the malady comes from a fracture, sprain or cautery, if you must make an incision, make a full incision around the hairs of paper; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent as I have said; and must be made according to the form of the malady, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive very well all sorts of things how to make return to their natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what must be done of work and instruments in various dispositions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this scab appears at home in a part as thin as the beard of a man, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, if you must, then drink the point of a rasp from the tip of your thumb and leave it in its place.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and keep it as tight as possible, as much as you can without making them too tight or too loose, so that the patient does not suffer from excessive pressure and does not vomit the oil
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision, which you have made, being as gentle as possible, so that the patient’s limb returns to its natural shape
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and is completely healed, and never again does any watery or dirty oil remain, and lift it with sweet water and vinegar.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	Then put between the paper and oil a wick of linen, and put on the oil wool felt in abundance.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And afterwards let the third part be dressed with a bandage and other soft things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	The nails are two ways:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	One is nervous and seems like iron two nails, and another which is not nervous, but seems like pale moisture frozen, that when it is touched with iron and is cooked in the pan, as many scratches appear as if it did not exist
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	And both seem to begin towards the great marrow, and cross each other so that they cover the whole cavity and the light and the movement of the oil
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And if the patient places his head in his throat, then hold the eyes;
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and hold the tongue at your hand, then grasp the jaw as if it were pierced by a small double, and stretch it upwards.
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put in hair of a horse, or of a cow, or of a bull, and tighten firmly.
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the point of the needle a little and fix it well in the jaw, and pierce with the needle and tie the jaw with a thread and stretch it upwards, and press all around the jaw with your fingers that support the cheek and the beard until the swelling subsides, and leave the natural discharge or saliva, if during the incision there is no discharge of tears usually
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	And never has the nail extended only at the cuticle, but as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	Then the swelling has spread over the whole nail bed as we have mentioned before.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	Keep the nail bed from touching the tough skin and break it, and do not notice the nail;
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	Then after the incision, pour on a some broth of broth onto the wound and sprinkle with lye, and leave it until the other evening.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then keep the wound clean as long as it is healing.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	If the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread will not go in, many times this semblance of a nail is cured by medicine;
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And they grow as I have said in the division; and if you see them covered, if you oil the patient, and take the gentler sponge according to this form.

des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes.

de la fistule de l’oil	And if you are unable to collect all this in that hour, if you make a poultice upon the oil of soothing things to ease the pain of the eyes, and leave it until the pain is appeased and is secured after the cautery, then begin again according to this method as long as you are well; and this is the way of forces: from the fistula of the oil.
