et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	if it is malignant pus, hasten and cauterize until it is dry and all the filth is gone, then throw or take out the bad blood or urine, easily and with pain or wine.</start_of_turn
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If it does not yield, and moisture comes up to the palate, urinate while sane.</start_of_turn
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if moisture does not go away as it should, urinate while it has pus in the bones above, because the subtle tremor comes from there.</start_of_turn>
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	When you must pull out a hair by its root, take a large loop of thread and pass it under the nail, and keep your hands steady, without leaving any space between the nails.
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	And put the patient’s hand over the hair by the root at the root of the nail, and grasp it firmly until it comes out through the nail hole in the mouth
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	And many times do the children make this mistake, and it is a light matter for him who sees it done;
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then take the part that comes by the nail in one hand, and the other part that comes by the mouth in the other hand, and grasp them one after the other while holding them close to us.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you are sure that the nails have not been damaged, then pull out the hair, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, and then reset the nail in its place as before
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	Do so for three days or more, until the oozing has corroded all that remains of the flesh. Then put in or remove a layer of wax for several days until it is healed, and if there is need of drying medicines, use them accordingly.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	This is the form of the instrument for extracting the head, in which we distill oils and medicines or not.</start_of_turn>
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And be of silver or gold, like a wide lamp, if like a chain, and guide it thus.</start_of_turn
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see, make a closed chain, and let the instrument be flat for purging the head.</start_of_turn
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And he has one hand clenched at the shoulder to hold it when we burn oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards on the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Many times there arises at the shoulder no disease which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large at will, until it is seen to be something.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	and therefore you must immediately support the limb at the beginning, and break the bone, then put out the fire or the burning medicine
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	and if you wait too long to support it when it is large, if you take warning that it is hard, of dark color, of poor sense:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	you must not touch it with iron for it is an inflamed abscess, for when it is supported even once, there comes great harm to the patient
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	If the swelling is soft to the touch, not of a dark hue, and you can see that it can be completely covered, if the patient vomits and groans in fear, and cures the limb of dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and bound over.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Make this until you know that they have not corrupted that hair, then bring the needle, wipe the blood, and moisten the needle in Egyptian fashion, and put it back in place as before; do this for three days or more, until the scab has corroded all that is remaining of the hair; and then put in or remove a cauterizing sponge for a few days until it is healed, and if there is need for calming medicines, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, from which we distill oils and medicines or the like.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	It is therefore necessary that this should not happen at all, if you see that the wound is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and immediately support both limbs at a brace, then treat until it is healed;
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	if the limbs are already dislocated from one side to the other, if you must support all the parts of their joints until they bleed, then reassemble the limbs at a brace, and strain, and sprinkle with dragon’s blood powder and incense powder
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place upon the wound a piece of gauze or another dressing that adheres, and leave it until it oozes by itself, then cure it of inflammation when it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	When the dislocation is thus set, if you rejoin the pieces,
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the treatment of wounds of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you before.
des apostemes des levres	of the separation of the layers of the skin.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	The hands often have within them the bones of the forearm split in two, like grains of wheat, minor and greater;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore you must turn the forearm, and make incisions above each bone, and grasp and fracture the parts apart
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	Then use the broth after the incision of the carbuncle, until the wound is closed;
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen the dressing and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la char des gencives	Concerning the pain of the jaws.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Many times it happens on the gums where garlic has been placed, which the old people call "albulus".</start_of_turn
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if you hold it firmly as it should be, and grasp the root, and leave the swelling or blood to escape;
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then put out the broth of the carbuncle, or other astringent and drying powders.</start_of_turn>
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if it comes back after the incision, and happens many times, if the root grasps it a second time, and cauterize it.</start_of_turn>
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	If it does not return naturally after the cautery.
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	And these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Never are they assembled at the head of the teeth, in the mouth between the gums, shields which are useful and rough
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	Never are the teeth black and yellow and soft, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting;
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	If you can make the patient sit between your hands, and his head is steady, and open the teeth or the shields until there is nothing left to do
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and so make blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other spots, until they are wiped off
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	And if the bone that is at the first root is sound, it is well;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if it is not sound, if it recurs again at the second joint and the third, until you have all healed;
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and the teeth that have mixed with various forms of instruments because of what it shows in the work, for indeed those that remove them from between the teeth have other shapes than those that are between the teeth
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these shapes and others will appear to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	You must know that when you treat the tooth from its pain, you must do it slowly and cautiously, for it must not make me do more harm
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	because it is a soft substance, therefore we have no excuse for making it bleed
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is constrained to endure, if you are certain that they will endure.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Many times the patient experiences pain, whether it be sudden or lasting, and makes the limb tremble.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and although it does not always depart with the pain, as long as the illness persists, for we have already made it suffer enough;
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	when you are quite certain that the pain is departing, if you are able, escort the limb at all times. Spread it out strongly to protect the limb from all sides.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	then put your hand on their shoulder or grasp the hair at the root and pull it out slightly, until it is well loosened, and then grasp it firmly again
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	and if the patient’s limb hangs between your thighs, hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, draw the tooth straight out towards the front; and if it does not come out immediately, take none of these instruments and hold it loosely in the cheek; and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the swelling is perceived and mixed, if you cover it with cloths, the wound or the hole will be open.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	and if the subtle strain has teeth, do not break them during the straining.</start_of_turn>
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	and you must say softly over the joint by pulling out the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave some, and return to the patient by the greatest pain of the first.</start_of_turn>
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	Be aware that you should not do this like the ignorant people, who by their haste and boldness break the limb every time and bring about nothing but what we have told you.</start_of_turn
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but they often bring about no remedy for the great disease by the roots that remain, or for the limb that is broken, as we have often said.</start_of_turn
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	And when the wound is dressed, if you bathe the limb with wine or oil and wool,
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	if blood comes out, as it often does, if you apply wine or oil and wool to the wound,
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The shapes of instruments, when they are mute at first, should have long points and broad handles, so that they do not break when you are drawing out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	These are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of great size if they do not bend when drawing, and be of fine iron well made, and be toothed so that they may hold firmly.</start_of_turn>
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth.</start_of_turn>
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root is stubborn when you are pulling it out, if you must put out the moist cotton swab in butter I or II, as long as the wound is bleeding, because that stops the pangs which are called “algophry,” for in this case the head of the shoulder seems like a beak of a sparrow
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And let the incisions be made thus as with a file, and thus is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not suffice to hold all these tensions, if you must uncover the marrow throughout the root, and put in the instrument which is called "althali", namely a palatine, for this is its form.
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And be strong and wide so that it does not break me, and if the root bursts through this, that is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, if you help with all your tools, so that the shapes come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument which has two rains, for this is its form
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And let these instruments be strong that they cannot break, and nails as thick as the nails of dense people
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	And like other instruments that are not counted here;
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And thus his masters know by themselves what instrument to choose, according to what his works and his disease show, for there are many diseases where the former did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of things; and if it breaks not from bone or from any other part, or if it hangs, if you search for instruments that you should choose, as I have said, and that you help with gestures, so that this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone, that it escapes not, but that you can hold and restrain.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Then restore the limb of medicine that is suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if the wound has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears does not match the natural curve of the jaw, and the shape is deformed, and even in women of childbearing age, if you must know that if you do not remove it when the tooth is loose, and it is not straight, you cannot heal it or support it
adonques lou raie;	Therefore, remove the bone;
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	And if it is with the tooth, take this instrument which has a small beak, and is like a pin, and be of iron without a groove in front:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And when the tooth persists in the gums and hands are clasped for a long time due to the duration of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you are using a file similar to this one which has the same shape.</start_of_turn>
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	And it is thus that we make needles as well.
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	And thus we hold the teeth firmly in place with our thumbs and index fingers, so that they do not move until they bleed
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	Then the limb at the end has no callous at all, and if it is too deep and bites the tongue, if you must keep the biting even until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or impede speech
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the front tooth is loosened, by percussion or by pressure, and the patient cannot press on what hurts except that it bleeds, and you must cure them with restrictive medicines, that does not work;
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if you must restrain them with gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and rusts, but the pain does not go away
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	And let the hair be neither too thick nor too thin, in accordance with the quantity of space between the teeth.
et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	And if you see the teeth leaning towards each other, if you take hold of the hair and double it between the two teeth that are closest together, then put the nails between the teeth next to each other until you see it is straight once more on the other side.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	Then repeat the covering until you reach the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and cautiously, until it does not move anymore.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	And let the suture be at the root of the tooth if it cannot escape
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then grasp the nails with pliers, assemble them and place them between the tooth and the tongue, and keep them in place so that the tongue does not bleed
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	Then he must leave it closed as much as he can, and if it slips, or if the thread breaks, if the strain of another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	if it should remain and hold it closed, and that is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two front teeth, and the two back teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth aches, if we put it back in its place, fresh and new, as we have said
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and there is no other thing that should intervene except for sage and balsam, and never make it the shape of a chipped tooth, and put it back in its place where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and it will remain closed for a long time
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Under no circumstances is this tongue or nature that comes from the nose, that we are born without.
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a deep wound.
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the work is such that you must offer the patient the mouth of the sick person, and put your head in his throat, and hold the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	then grasp the large nerve, until the tongue is detached from its seat, and if there is any delay or resistance, it is a sign of wound healing, if the ligature and the large nerve are loosened.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and take care that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that comes from the nose;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and when you have done this, if you lift the pale and easy or cold blood, then put the tongue back gently with a little tension;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	And the patient complains that at night his limb is stiff, so that he cannot rest.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	When blood comes out, if it brings forth a clot, take out the clot immediately.
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	And if it does not go away, burn it with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this purpose
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then treat it with other treatments until it is healed
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see pus of a color like blood or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is an abscess
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is declining with moisture, if there is moisture in it, if it is vomiting, and there is a visible swelling, and it delivers from both parts;
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	If it does not go naturally into its place, if put on a broken glass vessel until it is stained, then return to its place as long as you have treated everything else.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then lift the limb easily and cautiously, and treat it of other ailments until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
des apostemes de la gorge	From the throat apostemes.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Never comes from the throat lice which are called "godath," and they are properly two almonds; and when you treat them, as we said in the division, and they are not healed, beware.</start_of_turn
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is a tough abscess of small size and color, do not touch it with iron.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, even because of the discharge of blood.</start_of_turn
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it be until it is dead, and when it is so, you must take it away, or it will break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is of pale color and the root is flexible, if the instrument has appeared to cover it, but look first whether the abscess has calmed and is quiet.</start_of_turn>
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and that his arms be in their normal position, and cover his mouth and grasp his thumbs between his hands, and press the tongue down to the instrument, as it should be formed.</start_of_turn
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	And be of silver or of gold as subtle as a needle.</start_of_turn
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	Can you press the tongue down to the instrument, and you see the abscess, if you take the sponge and press it into the pus, and pull it out more than you wish.</start_of_turn
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	And take no thread from the cloth with, then place the cap over the instrument, for this is the form, that seems like one force.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And behold, the head of the sufferer is bent, one place with the other, and is very sharp, and is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have only a pair of tongs, know that this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	Or be split from one side and from the other side name;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have closed one of the wounds, if you close the other in the same manner, and afterwards make an incision, gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and remove the blood which comes out, if you gargle the patient with hot water, or there are blood clots which are cooked, or purples of mistletoe, and similar things, until the wound is clean
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then let the cure be until it is healed;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then let the cure be until it is healed; and never in the throat are there other abscesses born except for the two almonds, if the nails are thus left with the two almonds even.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was not in the throat, namely one abscess of small size
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had her well closed throughout the throat, so that she could neither breathe through the nose nor drink or eat, and died if she fainted in that state for even a moment or two
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so big that it had forced two stones out of its place twice.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I had done so much, and lay in one place, and the fire went out, and brought out large pieces of charcoal; and brought out a great portion of blood
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	Then pull out the other part through the other hole, and hold the mouth and press the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After placing the ointment on these abscesses, and closing a part, let only a little blood remain;
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and as soon as the blood vessel of the throat was loosened, and when she began to drink water and wine, and did not stop bleeding from this abscess for a long time
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and the abscesses reappeared in their place, filling the whole body as I had vomited violently, until it brought up large pieces of matter
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	therefore I grasped it and cauterized it inside the throat:
ensi demora sens croistre;	and like that I went away without saying anything more.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I depart from these parts, and only God knows what becomes of me after.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the limb hangs downwards, and it flees and is elongated, if it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is thick and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit me, and you see that the hair around the wound is quiet, and it is subtle, so you must cover it over
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and that which is round and gathered and is not long
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or dark-brown or black, so you must avoid the incision of the flesh
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.</start_of_turn>
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	You must therefore, when you see it, following the manner I have said, from its source and its length, make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument mentioned above.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then apply the ointment to the eye, and move it away, and hold it for two instruments as I have said concerning the incision of the two almonds.</start_of_turn>
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And must ensure that you do not cover more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit.</start_of_turn
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cover more, if he groans with his voice and his throat;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and afterwards the incision, use what we have said concerning the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, it must be known that you must use an engine for the cautery in the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of cautery must be gentle and not severe
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient puts his head in tone, and then he presses the tongue to the instrument which we have mentioned or the chapter of cautery, and grasps with live chaff, if it is neither too thick nor too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and with the use of this instrument, thus it is formed:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	Or he has a beard or one puts the medicine, as with the nails of a spoon, and puts the instrument over the wound
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the patient should be calm on his chest, so that saliva and mucus come out of his mouth from the medicine, if it does not go down to the throat, and he sneezes.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then keep your hand over the medicine and press it on the wound, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it callous and the bites of the medicine are appeased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see it, take hold and encircle it with any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and hold the instrument to its utmost extent within the joint above, until the cotton adheres to the limb.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	Do it often, until the burnings are perfect, then leave it dry, and cut after three days or five.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you must repeat the burnings from the medicine, when you repeat it, and after the burnings hold the eye well covered with cotton wool, and moisten what is around the medicine;
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the cold water be raised, and be cured of gargles as long as it is well.</start_of_turn>
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, for the cautery.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	This treatment is safer than incision, for the cautery. If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take chamomile, rue, origanum, camomile, ivy, and cloves, mix them all or some of them in a pot, put some oil in it, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well greased with strong earth, and in the pot has the instrument that is to be cauterized according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it can be of silver or gold, and the one of the bones is pricked in the patient’s mouth until the vapor reaches the eye by the smoke, until the eye is numbed.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	And repeat this often, until the eye is dry, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the emergence of the cautery, for many things happen;
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And do not make me do this for anything but the inclination of the afterburn.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a needle and put inside his head a piece of egg, so that the patient does not feel too much heat;
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the egg-shell does not make the vapor grow in the mouth, and this is a good cure altogether
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	Many times it has happened to me at the throat of bone or fish spine, or nothing at all;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	Therefore I advise you to do what you see, and press the tongue towards the sun with all the instruments, so that you can see the thing clearly
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what is not seen by me and is returned to the throat, I advise you to make the patient vomit immediately so that the meat is cooked in the stomach
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance, if this thing is vomited out whole;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patient swallows down a sponge, or a piece of rag, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and tie the sponge to the thread, and then transfix it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it comes out whole, if it is vomited, and then draw out the thread
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come out of its own, take an instrument of pliers as in this fashion:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	and let the instrument be curved at the head if it can enter more easily through the throat, and keep the head lifted;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and take care not to touch the epiglottis, that it does not bleed, do not break the bone inside
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	And the muscle is worth that the patient holds the instrument, because if it is moved or the thing is loose;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the thing falls down, or if it is forced strongly with all the instrument equally, as long as it is strong.</start_of_turn>
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the instrument curve at the head if it can enter more easily through the throat, with the head raised up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, for all will pass over it, do not push the bone inwards; and must it be known that the patient has held the instrument, for it is either that the thing is loose or that it is crooked; if the tongue swells, or if it is forced with all the instrument equally, as much as it is forced. From the absence of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Never is medicine without blood, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines.</start_of_turn>
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when this does not help, then look at the patient’s throat in the sunlight, and then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.</start_of_turn
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the armpit, if the wound has even a small lump, or if you suspect that there are subtle tensions that are worth as much.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that is not the case, take a pinch of caine and put it in the patient's throat, then press or pinch the caine lightly until it is burned, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient groans with acute pain all over
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full water to see if it is cold, and cover the mouth, and vomit in the direction of swallowing, and move the hand often.</start_of_turn
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And if you touch it without feeling pain, even if it aches.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not ache as we have said, if you suspect the patient is affected with madness, with the instrument which I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do it often, for it will make sense to target
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of fumigation is that you take one pot or there are charcoal pieces, and that you cover the area with a gauze cloth about a mile wide, and in that hole you make the hole of the instrument
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then I pour the fumigation, and the patient puts the tip of the cannula in his mouth, closes his mouth so that the smoke does not go out, but comes out only through the nose
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	And now the patient cries out, and if she does not desist, we must fumigate her repeatedly.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and she drinks foul and dirty things, and does not drink water;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	therefore she must be forced to vomit by this treatment.</start_of_turn>
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the form of the instrument with which we treat the patient, if it is seen, is like a pair of tongs with teeth to enter the throat.</start_of_turn
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	it has the shape of a goose beak, and has the roughness of lime, so that whatever she grasps, she cannot let go.</start_of_turn
et vez ci la forme:	And thus is the shape.</start_of_turn>
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	The wounds of an abscess are like those which are remembered to come after one thing and another in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and there are two ways in which one is like the other, and the other from moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And thus if it is for the limbs or if they are at the bone.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling at the head is different from that at the root, and the swelling at the bone is different from that which comes at the joints, and the nails have their own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if abscesses are not to be pierced, as long as the swelling subsides according to its course;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	if there are some which must be pierced when hardened, and do not subside naturally according to their course, like abscesses which are between joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when swelling comes from the joints, and it is left as it is until it is bruised, by chance if the bone and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of this there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	or if the abscess is between the principal limb, and you delay the perforation until it is measured, it will be done to the principal limb;
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	When the fire is applied at the root, if it is withdrawn before it has died down, it will be useless.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And I advise you only that you pierce with the fire only when the digestion is complete, for the one that is withdrawn from the root must not be pricked, but must remain along its course, and there will be no fistula formed
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and will not heal in great measure
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	I advise you that you should withdraw the fire from the incision when the pain has subsided, the swelling has gone down, the fever has receded, the pain and redness have ceased, and there is no debate or discomfort about the progress of the incision or other signs
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and that you hold the incision or more stable according to the progress of the abscess, and where there is movement of the bone.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Or let the wound be made on a long limb, and if the edges of the wound are with hands or pieces, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and all be even, or there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the limb itself.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the opening is in the flesh, if it is confirmed during digestion as we have said
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you prick before this, if it runs along the limb from it, and there is plenty of pus;
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance toughen the flesh and deepen from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no wound that is perceived according to the large wound, according to what the limb has to bear.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	So must you bring many small wounds, small incisions.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in great incisions, great wounds, and many cuts according to the greatness of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if there are such abscesses or it must be feared that the limb will be deformed, and covered;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When the eye has become swollen like a drooping drape, and is softened, if you wish, you can do the same as for bubbles.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are those that are split into three angles, and those that can be grasped like the fennel flower, like abscesses of grapes;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are those for which you make a round the size of a plum, and other sizes and similar things.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who have no head, if like a superficial abscess, you must simply pierce them
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and when the abscess is large, and it has caused great swelling, and you pierce it, do not remove all the swelling at once, but only a part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then I stamp the abscess up to the other ear, and then do nothing further.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this many times with great force, until the swelling is completely gone
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Even if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a young boy, or an old man decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if it is small, look to see if the abscess has come out of the wound
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a large wound, mix together lint or old cotton
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if there is a great abscess and there is much pus, you must bite in the cheek with a cloth so that one covers the other
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	If you have cauterized in the abscess a part of raw leather, and you have shut it in the flesh, you must know that you must fill it up with much cotton or coarse thread of flax towards moisture, and keep it there until the third part of the joint.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the bone, and cure the swelling until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood should discharge from your work, order cold water and ease, and moisten the bandage, and draw out the offending part many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the discharge of blood persists, mix with government and cure, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is too late, and the wound or abscess is moist nervous, if you can, put on a bandage and moist cloths soaked in wine and oil
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is late, and the wound is fleshy, if you can, put on moist cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and oil, until the third part of the joint, as we have said
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove the abscess, drain it, and cure it if possible, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	It is known throughout that it is successful in treating abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have said before, you must alert before treating abscesses, and thus it will be successful.
des soros	indeed
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or indeed, from the chief comes a little abscess, and it is a custom of us that it is in silks, like the blossoming of a hyacinth, and there is resemblance in it.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that have fat and those that have moisture just like pus;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if there are some that are tough and hard at the root, and there is no doubt that the artery does not oppose it
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And concerning the work of the size, if you expect with all the instruments which are called "entromissoire", from which the shape comes afterwards, what thing does it contain?
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if you make it through with long doubs.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	When the moisture is drained, if you leave the peel that contains that moisture, it will return as before
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then plunge cotton into the Egyptian eye, if it is present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If it is not there, in water and oil, and apply the bandage, and leave it until the other side is healed.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And this will correct what is delayed due to pain
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And thus repeat the cotton, as before, the second time, and the third, until you are certain that it does not remain painful;
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of the eye when it is convenient, until it is healed
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess persists without fat, if it is cut according to this form, for a long time
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and let your sponges flow, and the pus from all parts, and put all your cure to drain towards the navel or where it is placed
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the artery opposes you, do as I have said afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with the fistula if it is perforated, and cut and cure as I have told you before
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the perforated abscess and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are matters of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	If there is no swelling or moisture in these abscesses or swellings, and if they do not yield to pressure from an old woman’s hand, I cauterize or extract them.
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	I find the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and cannot burst it
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if no blood flows from it, we must make a wound as deep as a stone
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses of the vein or bone, because these things come from the head and root of the ear, they burst immediately if they are not opened from the first day of their existence, for fear of bursting the belly
et les cure si com il covient.	And the treatment is as he commands.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times it happens that the abscess comes out at the collarbone, and the armpits, and under the arm, and never from any other place or bone, and is bloodstained, and is enclosed with blood clots
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And if a swelling appears in the armpit, near the armpit and the incision of the head, as we have said; and the appearance of these swellings is many.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And if any swelling is properly within its sheath, if it does not move and is sutured at the root, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And the signs of these swellings are many
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In such a case as this, where you see a good arrangement of bones at the touch, and it is similar in color to bone, and is soft from one side and does not bleed from the artery or vein, nor is it deep; if you must break it, you must do so from below, and burn the soft part, and elevate the two levers of the forearm as we have mentioned in the apostemes of the head; and hold the thumb and index finger still so that you do not damage the nerve or vein, and do not cause swelling or bruising, except for the hand itself, and do not raise it too high before you have closed.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in those where you see a good position at the touch, and is similar in color to coral, and moves only from the swelling part and not from the head or the artery or the vein, and is not deep
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it can be grasped by the nails and the swelling part is scorched, and if two fingers of the hand are placed as we have said in the incisions of the head;
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And the way to proceed is thus: do not cover the nerve or the vein, and do not let the splinter or the nails escape, but keep the hands steady and do not speak too much, for you must not cover anything that you are not to cover.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	If you cover the vein or the artery, and this does not allow you to work, if you put in the wound a bit of vitriol broken or some powders that remain inside, and constrain the wound;
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	leave it until the spasms are calmed and the wound is softened, and then begin to move.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the thing is stained, if you return to your work until you have completed it;
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then you must know that you must indicate that there are no small scabs, that you must cope and bind them
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is in the root of the scrophule a great swelling, if it will not suffice to cope only with that scrophule at its root, but bind with a strong double thread and leave it in its place, as required.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	Then apply the wound closure of white cotton steeped in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	if you understand to cover the root of the [disease] and drain away the pus, and close it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas which keep swelling, pierce them or they will die; and pierce them as before said, according to the circumstances, then mix with oil and similar things, so that it destroys what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, if the oil cure has taken hold of the char, as long as it is sane.</start_of_turn
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulae which maintain excessive swelling, pierce them or they will open and die
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and pierce like the one mentioned before, depending on the case, and mix sponges with ointment and similar things, so that it may cleanse what is remaining of corruption

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old men spoke of the size of the gorge; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the writing of their words.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The old people spoke and told of the size of the gorge;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen in our land anyone who has done it, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	As for those who are squinting, it is necessary that the gullet which is called the epiglottis be cut away;
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and this does not help, for all the veins and the blood vessels of the patient are at those which have been cauterized in the mouth, or in the throat or in the armpits.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary therefore, when our wounds are about to burst the epiglottis, to cut them from three circles or four, a small incision through two circles or by the amount of the incision on the surface, not through the cartilage; and if it is necessary to join the epiglottis with the section of the epiglottis that there is no char, and the blood vessels are long enough.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is necessary therefore, when we cut the epiglottis, to cut from three circles or four a small cut through, between the two circles or by the quantity of the cut of the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And thus if it is necessary to break the cartilage at the epiglottis, there is no char [foreign body] there, and the vessel is long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is doubtful, then it is right to extend the skin of the throat to its utmost extent, then cut through the skin as far as the chin;
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And evacuate the blood vessels, if you see nothing else, and then close the wound as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	It is shown by the section of the voice that the leap would jump out by the broken bone, and by the absence of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	When the hour has passed since the dislocation, if there is still doubt about the strangulation, join together the two levers of the wound of the chin, and bind them all together so that the cartilage is held in place;
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then administer medicines that cause the formation of pus, as long as they are safe.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore close the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe; and he breathes through the wound; and thus is preserved from death; and for this reason the ancients command that the old man leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they command that the wound be closed and healed, until it is healed; and I shall tell you what I have seen.
