Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a lady had taken a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of her windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I fled called for help, and found her just like death.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and closed the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and the lady did not feel any pain, and returned to her normal state; for in the handling of the epiglottis, I did not find any fear
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and bound up the wound, and cured it until it healed completely.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and did not leave the patient without speaking to her, and returned afterwards to her usual state
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I know that in the case of a strangulation of the epiglottis, I have no fear
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "neck hernia," and are great abscesses of a yellow color, and are very common in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally there is no cause.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This swelling is called "hernia of the throat," and is a large swelling of a yellow color, and is very common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and there are two kinds:
naturez, et accidens;	natural, and accidental
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or the natural one has no cause
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the cause of the accident is in two ways, for one is similar to fat, and the other manner is similar to an abscess coming from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is doubt, and one cannot safely work without fear except in this case, and it proves and seeks all the surrounding tissues:
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it like that, with no fat, and cannot touch any vein, if you grasp it, as we grasp the testicles, and pull at all its circumference, if there is no point there
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then you must tightly embrace all around, and cure it as if it were sane.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways of us are, of which I will speak of all; and behold that I tell you all the difference which is between health and sickness.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways for us to be like this, of which I will tell you all the resemblances.</start_of_turn>
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And thus it is known that I tell of all the difference which is between a nut and a bolt.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that dislocation is a swelling and fever lasting as long as the boils are not passed, and is accompanied by swelling
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	therefore rest the fever and the swelling.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without nut there is neither fever nor swelling nor pain, and contains its own sac, which is its own colour, and begins like a fatty substance, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and resemble butter, or grease, or moisture, and moisture of a yellow colour as I have said in the division
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of the inquiry of abscesses of us is that you take more moisture from the root than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs and fingers, until you know that the instruments have perceived the mark; then that it be according to the greatness of the abscess; then draw out the entrament, and take care that the spur does not bleed
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of questioning abscesses of the bones is that you take more moisture from the bone than you find in the abscess, and turn your thumbs and big toes inward until you perceive that the marrow has sensed the pain, and that this is according to the size of the abscess
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then take away the entraumissor and beware of the sudden jerk.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	When moisture covers it completely, as it has been mentioned previously regarding other incisions;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after removing the entraumissor no more moisture appears, although it was fat previously, if you pierce it, take hold with tweezers and burn away the surrounding area with a bit of soot, taking care not to burn the coat where you are working with the needle;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If you do not manage to remove it completely, if you pull out pieces, nothing will remain.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, it will come back many times again;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there is still some remaining, and it does not trouble you, if you apply corrosive powders and hold the wound firmly, and put soothing things on the wound above, and treat it with other cures until it is healed
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it is great, if it costs two pounds of the wound, and cure it of what fills it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	And if the wound bursts against you or another, if you are in a hurry and use powdered vitriol, leave it for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the bloodletting;
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to the covering that has been delayed by now.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See here the forms of the entrapped instruments, and there are three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	Large, medium, and small
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	And there are three quarters that are called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and there are three ways of doing it
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Great, medium, and small, to encompass the fistulas of abscesses.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	They are like needles which we extract from wounds, and are of saffron, or iron, or silver, and must be strong enough to hold those which are yellow, and are more proven by black soot to encompass the curves of the fistula.
et sont de III manieres:	They are of three kinds.
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of these needles resemble mustard seeds, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	Great, medium, and small
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if the needles have two curves of three kinds also;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	And if there are three curves and are also of three kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	And if there are two curves and there is only one curve remaining, and there are three kinds of curves.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	All these curves are necessary for their substance.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these bones is thick, and there are some which do not break through the skin but only on one side, from which we strip the hair, because of this we do not touch the vein or the nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these inward protrusions are the bones that are returned in sleeves, so that the patient does not lose them when the incisions are made
et sont de III manieres:	There are three kinds of these bones.
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Great, small, and medium, if you see it;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	Great, small, and medium, if you see it; do not use it elsewhere but in the joints, as in the leg, arm, shoulder, elbow, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never make use of any other small instrument, like the knuckles of fists, in this fashion, as it will obstruct blood flow.</start_of_turn
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Blood does not swell in the breasts of many patients when they begin to fester, so that they seem like breasts of a woman; and they become heavy and limp, and those who see them will believe they are cured, if they are treated according to this form from line b to g.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never swell the breasts of some men when they are about to become corrupted, until they appear like the breasts of a woman.</start_of_turn
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and endure pain and boils, and who sees them cured, if it can be cured in this fashion from line b to line g.</start_of_turn
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape away the fat, and use the medical plaster thickly spread, and sew up the wound with stitches; and cure it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	When the breast swells down and is relieved by its great size, as with women, if the wound is within two ribs below, by two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	So that one holds the greater line against the lesser one, so that the greater line contains the lesser one in this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.;

et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if he is not sound, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient cannot rest, or for the discharge of blood, if you must, fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive order.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it has consumed the remnant and the fat, then cure it until it is sound again.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come from the buttocks are managed by hard scrofula or if there are ribs, and there is only moisture inside.</start_of_turn
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	If there is moisture contained, it must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When any swelling is in the apostem, if one employs the wound of fine cotton, and leaves it until the other side, then bind up all the cotton, and cure the wound that comes from that as long as it is sound.</start_of_turn>

de la routure de l’artere	From the root of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	If the artery is blocked, and the skin is swollen above, if there are many abscesses, or if the vein is burst and abscesses occur; if the surgeon knows that it is for the artery, if the abscesses are large enough to obstruct the passage of the hand; and if he knows that it is for the vein, if there is excessive bleeding around the edges; it is foolish to close this abscess, even if it has burst the testicles and caused swelling and pain in the groin and other parts of the body, and is great.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin is split which is above, if there are many abscesses again, and also there is blood escaping from the vein and from the rupture;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you know that this is due to the artery, if the abscesses are large and protrude significantly.</start_of_turn>
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you have known this, if you know it is stretching;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when it comes to the vein, if it is rehearsed to flee from its opening;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	And when it comes to the vein, if it is rehearsed to flee from its opening, it is foolish to cover this incision, and even more so when it is full of blood clots and abscesses, or other bones, and there is great pain.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	One must therefore avoid the treatment of fire, and he who is at the head must also avoid it, and in the one who has a swelling of an artery has done by the above the skin along the length.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then one must uncover the size as one can, and depart well the artery from its covering, until it is uncovered;
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then one must take hold of the blood clot with an awl, and make it bleed until it reaches the other edge, and strain the artery with a doubled thread in two places, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples;

puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then bring the cure that sustains the bow, as long as it bites;

puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then bind the aponeurosis, as I have said, or ligate it with two threads of the same kind;

puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	Then cauterize the surrounding area until the pus comes to the surface, then cauterize the pus until it is black, and leave only what is bound;
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on a wet cloth soaked in wine and oil, and mix with cures of sponges and poultices until it is healed.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Then put upon one drape of moist cloth in wine and oil, and mix with cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often occurs in cases of attendants and those who must endure them or in all limbs where there are joints, and it is I grieve abscesses, and its colour seems like the colour of honey, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when it is strained, if it causes pain to the patient, it is not like honey, but like blood; and it swells very much from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, neither upwards or downwards, and that which is in the joints cannot be covered with iron: by chance there will be contraction; and he who is head or neck or brow, will burst the skin at the hairline.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this often happens with adjuvants and must be treated with care in the joints or in other places, and this is the cause of many post-operative deaths, and its color is like that of saffron, and is in many other situations accompanied by pain
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is strained, if the patient feels pain, and does not wish to endure any more pain, but desires to depart, let him go out.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	He must remain perfectly still in all parts, neither going forward nor backward, neither to the left nor to the right, neither up nor down, and he who is in the joints must not be bound by iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	because there will be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is at the head or the shoulder or the front, makes the skin taut around the nail
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, if he has one tooth remaining, and grasps it at the root
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is large, if the cavity has pus, and it is burned, and the bone is fractured, and the wound is closed at the suture, and the cure is made as long as it is healthy
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never have I seen such swellings elsewhere as in the belly; it is a disease which is called "funge" because of its resemblance to worms, and its root is subtle, and its head is large; and there are small and great ones. I have known of two bellies which appeared more like funguses than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thick root, and were ulcerated at the bottom.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	Never have I seen such a thing in the belly and nowhere else, and it is a disease which is called "funge" because of its resemblance to a worm, and its root is subtle, and its head is large.

Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them out and found in one XVIII ounces and in the other VI and a half, and the work in the incision if you look to see if the patient is moist is white and bloody and has a thick root
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	If the shoulder hangs loose and hangs large, and you are in my presence, I order the cautery of fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For at that time there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if you do not delay, if you do not hasten, then indeed you must cauterize.</start_of_turn>
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	And if you see the patient groaning and fearful from the incision of the wound, if you take a thread of silk well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days.</start_of_turn
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	Then the restraint, and do not cease to tighten the thread of silk until it holds the artery, and ask from him what he feels;

puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then treat the wound, and keep that you do not cover the hair which is of coarse color and poor sense and yellow milk.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the shoulder joint is inflamed.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If a boil appears, it comes by burning of the wound or incision of the abscess, and is on the belly and there are some pus, as it happens in other ways, or blood that clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or swelling; and if it is through the abscess and through the issue of the bowel, if it is the color of the afterbirth resembling the color of cheese, and is a light thing with little pain, and opens with various issues.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	Then if pus appears, it comes from cautery of wound or incision of abscess, and is above the belly and in the flanks, as it happens in other ways, or blood that clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or of windgrittiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is through the opening of the abscess and the discharge of pus, if its color is like that of the post, it is a light matter causing pain, and is an open wound of various discharges.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is by moisture, it is a light matter; open it well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain me; and if it is by blood, if it is opened by these signs, the abscess is great and hard, and is filled according to a quantity; and if it is by wind, if it is blown upon the touch, and the work is that you must observe whether it appears to be by the blood of an artery or a vein, or the wind.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and opens well when you press it with your hand, do not restrain me;
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is for blood, if it is wide open by these signs, the abscess is great and hard, and is closed according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, if the toucher is soft, and the work is that you see if it appears due to the blood of an artery or a vein, or moisture.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or in this chapter concerning abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If it appears to be by intestine or swelling, instruct the patient to hold his breath, and when he has exhaled completely, then mark around the swelling with your finger; then command him to grasp your hands together, and extend the limb that you have marked at all its joints; then pull the limb that is opposite to the swelling a quarter of its way; then bind it firmly with a strong thread or strong silk cord, and hold it in place; then uncover half of the swelling and place your index finger and the thumb over it; if you find the intestine caught in the binding, if you pull it out, let go of the swelling and bring the intestine back through the navel; if you find the swelling, if you grasp it at the navel and squeeze out the excess; if the artery opposes this, or the vein, if it is going well, then return to your work and take two needles, and pass two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have done in the shape that you think you will pierce; then strain the swelling for three days over the needles, and if you see that it is over, break the needles, and leave the limb as long as it swells, and cut off the dead tissue by itself; or you can cauterize it when it is small and soft, and cure the limb of what is necessary, and keep the swelling as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the limb of what is necessary, and bandage the limb.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if it appears from the intestine or the bile, then you must command the patient to hold his breath, and keep it extended, and then mark around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then command him to grasp between your hands, then go around the limb that you have marked at all the circumference, then pull half of the abscess downwards to the greatest extent
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then he binds it around a strong thread, or a strong silk cord firmly, and let us know if it is secure.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then he stretches half of the abscess outwards on the limb, and under that he must place the index finger, and the thumb;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it grasped by the limb, if you loosen it, and bring the intestine away from the belly
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bone fractured, if you grasp it at the edge, and cut off the surplus
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or the vein has been injured, if it is bleeding excessively, then go back to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you have made in the form of a cross that you make pierce
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then strain the abscess in four days upon the needles; if you see it, break the needles, and leave the wound open until it bursts, and take the dead matter away by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you can put it in when it is small and soft, then cure it of what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said before.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	Drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound of what is necessary, and suture the wound
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the signs of a boil, and how it should be treated with medicines, and how it should be avoided; and we say that a boil swells in the marrow, and has great caution in its cure, and that the old men say that when a boil is in the bone or can be pulled out like a boil that is in marrow, and in the flesh, and similar things, and that it must be removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is great and old, if you do not approach it, for I do not know that it can be cured; nor has anyone ever cured it before me.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the preceding chapters about the signs of abscess, and how one should work on them with medicines, and how one should shun the cautery treatment
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	We say that an abscess is dangerous in the marrow, and great caution should be used in its treatment, and they say that the old people often leave an abscess open when it is in the bone or can be drained if it is pus-filled, and in swelling, and similar things, and that one must remove it entirely when it is in its beginning
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	And when it is large and old, if you do not approach it cautiously, for I know of no cure;
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	for I know of no cure in such a case.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	When it is in the flesh or we can remove it, as we have said, you must never purge the black bile from the patient.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make him healthy if he shows excessive fullness, then remove the cause of the ailment gently;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then drain your abscesses or carbuncles, and the head of all parts, and the bone of all parts together, leave nothing untouched
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow freely, and keep your hand or anything else away from it, and if it bleeds excessively from the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize as much as necessary without staining
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of other wounds as long as they are healthy.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be trenchant from two parts.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have already mentioned in the division the signs of dropsy, and that when the collection of water is made, and the signs of swelling appear, and the treatment made by medicine, and that which is cured by fire.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only slightly darkened;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one must not touch fire in these two signs:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	that is to say, tympanites and hypothermia, because it is a deadly thing
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	then when you give these medicines for this sign which is called "eclites" of medicine, and the cure does not benefit, if you notice that the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, as for example vomiting and diarrhea, and similar things;
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If there is doubt, do not touch the iron, for fear of further danger.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	If you see the patient with great strength, and he has no other illness except for hydrophobia alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, if you must work on him.
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Believe the patient right on your hands, and press the belly outwards towards the lower part of the gut, then take the bony spine in this fashion:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver needle, with a head of lead or barley lighter, and on the lower part there is a little hole; and on one side there are three holes, and two on the other side, and one on the other side; and the head of the pin is cut off like a penknife. This is the form of incision which they write with the penknife.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Pointed, and do not be so violent that it can come as far as the intestine when you insert it, and do not stain it
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	Then look if hydrophobia is hanging towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	If you think you have reached the bottom of the third bone, put two fingers on the navel
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	And if dropsy is due to liver disease, if so make a incision on the left side of the belly at the third rib.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	And if it is due to urine, if so make an incision on the right side, and do not let the patient lie on the incision until the urine has ceased to flow from that weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce through the skin with an instrument, and remove the stone, and keep your hand over the area between the skin and the bone as if grasping the quantity of an nail or as if cutting into an ear
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the bone until the callous comes out, and that is the cause of the pain, then draw out the instrument, and that is the end of the treatment.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	It is like a silver needle, and is of lead or charcoal lighter, and has on the lower part a small hole
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	And if cost from one side, three parts;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	And if cost from one side, three parts; and two from another side, and one from another.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And the head of the shoulder is torn like a quill, and this is the form of the incision which they write to cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	At the top is the marrow, so that when the instruments come into pain, if they now descend above the instrument;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty half or a third part, for if you empty more than that which can be contained in this hour, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the wound, or he will bleed profusely, or he approaches death
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but emptying according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the provisions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse;
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	Then take the instrument and hold the liquid, which is now retained by the spur that is above the socket as I have said; pierce according to this manner.
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	Then take the instrument again, the other way round, if you see the patient suffering this, and pour a little liquid;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Do nothing of the sort, and keep using as much liquid as necessary until the bleeding stops.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you are uncertain about the patient, and you give him too much liquid, if the surgeon of the burial or sand burn, and by giving him sweat or bath and sun, and if you are careful to drink;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the surgeon of medicines should dry him out until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extracting the liquid, as I have said before
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If he persists so much that he does not perceive all that is around him very attentively, following this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or prick the soft flesh of the groin, and bind and hold it for three days or four, and when he wants to urinate, if he is kept closed, he will urinate and then return it; and by chance he cannot do this, because the urine that comes out will not leave him closed
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening of the wound is small, if it is treated with ointment of lead, as we have said, if it expands.
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	Then put or draw out I clo subtil of urine, and bind and hold it for III days or IV, and when it wants to urinate, if it be held close, urinate, and then put it back.
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	And by chance it cannot be, for the urine that comes forth will not leave it closed.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the shoulder and the scapula as wide as a thumb, if the mark pricks in the middle, as it should; and you keep from discharge of blood which comes many times, and if it comes, if the stain of this blood which stains blood, and cure the wound until it is healed.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the passage at the root of their thigh are blind, for none are born who have the passage at the head of the thigh, for they cannot urinate before they have raised their thigh high
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	and cannot urinate except for that the matter cannot come down to the navel, and it is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of this work is that if the patient lies supine on his back, with the head of the thigh and the buttock as large as a thumb, if the passage is in the middle, as it should be;
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave the blood alone when it comes many times; if it does stain, keep the dressing of that which stains blood, and heal the wound while it is sound.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is festering, of a bad colour and discharging pus, it is necessary to apply cautery to it.</start_of_turn>
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	Many times blood comes out in this part, and it is a sign of bad blood;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	There are both malignant and non-malignant causes of this.</start_of_turn>
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	If it is suspected that the cause is slight, then one must give a slight incision, and then grasp and pull out all the black matter, and then put on Egyptian cotton over it.</start_of_turn
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the wound while it is sound.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cure it altogether, if it is not firmly secured, the head of the shoulder will be perceived [as loose]; and blackness and corruption will ensue in its root or head; if you cover all that is black and corrupted, then apply above it a plaster made of honeycomb and flour, which is made from the peel of pomegranate seeds and sometimes, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have grasped it, and if the blood is still in the vein, and has partly gone into the belly and partly outwards, if it is suspected that the blood is in the vein first.</start_of_turn
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When he is soldered, if the doctor flees.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	When you hold him together, if he does not feel secure, if his limb is grasped too tightly, there will be blackening and corruption of the limb or the flesh;
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you must crush everything that is black and corrupted, then lie on the place of honey and flour which is made of pomegranate peel and sometimes, then the doctor must make other cures until he is healed
de la circoncision	from the circumcision.</start_of_turn>
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery is useful in two situations when he is soldered together.
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	namely, at the discharge of blood and at the corruption of the flesh.
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the limb is corrupted and retracted, if you must bite or draw out the limb a bundle of hair, and urinate the patient among the wounds;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And when the hair has grown to the root of the beard which is on those who have not had them circumcised, or if there is a wound or incision, if you must then stretch it with the instrument which is called a tweezers, until the hair is loosened from its root; deliver the hair from the beard in all parts.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	And if this is the cause of discomfort, if you must stretch it with the spatula, do not touch the root of the beard or the hair
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then dry it thoroughly between two, and put one fine towel of linen wet with cold water on it, which must not be wrinkled
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us circumcision, for they did not use it in their law, and we have learned only what we have learned through experience
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not like other wounds;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	although when we make this work of our will, and as well as possible, if it is necessary that our work be more perfect and lighter for health.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and physicians who performed circumcision around the navel and had force and all the instruments;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if they fled the urine because there are two towels there, and by chance if one covers this one and leaves the other behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	or it covers the wound, and the pain is doubled, and the swelling which is under the navel is not securely held at the point of the limb;
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and the swelling of the bone by chance escapes the wound, and repairs the work, and many times they are born again until they have no need of swelling and I desire it.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the wound is like this: the two fingers should be tense and firm, and the fingers should be as great as the thumb equally:
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if it is equally tense throughout, the soul tension;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	But let the thread be well strong and twisted about the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	But let the thread be well strong and twisted about the skin; and if you make the child think that you are doing it, if he understands, do not force him to hold the thread only at the root, but do make him hold it all the way around as much as possible.</start_of_turn>
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then do make him hold it straight between your hands, and bring the forces together between your hands or pull out your pieces so that the child does not see them, neither any of the instruments.</start_of_turn
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then hold your hand to the root and breathe or groan, and pull up as much as the head of the shoulder is engaged.</start_of_turn
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then thoroughly wipe away the filth that is gathered; then tie the limb with a double thread, and tie it well with another thread.</start_of_turn>
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	And the thumb has two double bonds at the second phalanx and the base of the index finger, and overlaps between the two lines, then seize the nail downwards heavily and draw out the head of the nail.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow freely downwards and outwards, for this is the way of the wise men.
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and over the powder I drape a cloth glued with a piece of rosebud gum boiled in oil, fragrant with rosemary leaves, and leave it on until the other side is healed, and treat the other wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The forces of the limb are softened in this manner.</start_of_turn>
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	the two thumbs should be tense and firm, and the fingers as great as the palm equally.</start_of_turn
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of the mundane if it is when the hair grows at the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore, you must extend it at your nail, so that it will not cause incision again.</start_of_turn>
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and keep it even, and if you do not keep hold of your nail, if you let go, and then hold it again.</start_of_turn
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if it persists for three days, and that which is beside the belly is inflamed, if you leave it as long as the swelling subsides, and burn it gently.</start_of_turn
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	if you move it as you please, and keep hold of the belly, it will do no good.</start_of_turn
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore, cure the wound with powdered things like we have said or treat with powders, and if you move it too much, it will go down, and will do no good.</start_of_turn
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Heal the wound, as we have said, until it is healed.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus the method of extracting urine is as follows: if you take a double thread and tie one end to the chief of wool or cotton, and pass the thread through the tube; and press out the surplus of wool and pass until you reach the chief of the tube, then join the tube with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair; and raise the bladder and the testicles with oil moist and oily, and water tepid; then put the tube gently into the testicle, until it reaches the root of the testicle; then double the testicle towards the buttock; then pull out the tube before it reaches the bladder, and make the patient feel it come out until it is empty; this must not be done except in this order for that which it leads or goes is turned; then cut the thread at both ends and the urine will follow the thread, and withdraw it forcefully, and correct the urine; and repeat the tube until the bladder is empty, and be sure the patient is aligned.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The urine is retained if there is an obstruction of the stone, or of blood clot, or of bile, or of worms, or similar things, as we have mentioned in the previous part.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	If the urine is not discharged, and you see that the obstruction is caused by the stone which is in the belly or the neck of the bladder, then you must assume that the patient is hunching over his knees
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	And put the hand over the back, extend the abdomen from the upper part of the back, and restrain the patient so that he does not move as much as he can
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	Then hold the neck of the bladder towards the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is discharged easily
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, if you must, administer extraction with all the instruments that are called "syringes," for this is the form.
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	Or of thin, soft silver wire, like the quill of a bird.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Or of a thorn of a length and a half, or of soft metal at the head
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of extracting urine is that you take two threads doubled, and bind one at the head with a loop of wool or cotton, and pass the thread through the syringe.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And drain the excess of wool and hold the syringe until the patient sits on the seat, and then raise the bladder and the testicles with oil and olive oil and warm water
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then insert the syringe gently into the vein, until it reaches the root of the vein, then double the vein upwards towards the bulge.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then pull back the syringe until the patient feels the blood coming back to the empty part, and that is not done except in the order which is necessary for the purpose; for in this way it is known whether it will succeed or fail.</start_of_turn>
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then hold the thread taut at all times, and the urine follows the thread, then draw out the thread, and do the same with the urine.</start_of_turn
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And start the syringe again until the bladder is empty, and the patient is comfortable.</start_of_turn>
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two from one side, and one from the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped so that the medicine can be placed as well as possible on the limb, if we can remove the moisture, and push as much as necessary; and when you see the medicine dripping from the bladder, put the chief of the doctor in the moisture, and pull at the one who is holding. If you pull the moisture from the holder, and then push it back strongly; if the moisture enters the holder, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and that is the form of the subtle cluster from which we cluster the bladder: if this is the case:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	It is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from one shoulder or the other; then take a bladder of mutton and put the moisture which you see clustering the bladder inside it, then bind it between the two shoulders with a double bow; and burn one of those moistures on the fire; then withdraw the chief of the cluster from the limb, and stretch your hand over the bladder with all the moisture coming out, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round; then draw the thread strongly through these holes, and assemble the circle as if assembling a ball, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and bind it with the instrument; and do as if you had made a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if there are three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	I on one side, and I on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	I on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and if the patient grasps his chest with both hands, as we can bear with difficulty the moisture, and pushes when the matter is urgent, then…
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	…and when you see the physicians shivering in the belly, put the head of the sufferer in the moisture, and push whatever is in the way.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you push out the moisture at the root, and then push strongly the thing that is in the way…
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	if there enters moisture into the wound, and comes to the belly now, so that the patient will feel it;
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	and this is the form of a subtle blister from which we must blister the belly.
si est ci:	If it is thus:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	If it is thus: and it is of silver or gold, and the head is higher;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	and the nails are drawn to the skin or the bones are fractured
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	then take a bladder of mutton and put the moisture which you see collecting in the bladder, then bind it between the two armpits with a double thread, and burn that moisture on the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	then draw the head downwards towards the armpit, and hold your hand over the bladder until all the moisture has drained out, until the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around the circumference
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	Then I pull the thread firmly through these holes, then I assemble the circle as if I were assembling a ball, and I put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and I tie it in the instrument.
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And do as if you had made a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is incarcerated in the bladder often causes vomiting, which is a sign that the stone is pressing on the bladder almost as much as in its entirety; and there is frequent vomiting, gravel in the urine, pain in the side, and many times the patient is unable to urinate, and then becomes constipated; and from these vomiting attacks the foundations are loosened.  The cure for these vomiting attacks is more gentle in young people than in old people, and is more effective in those between youth and old age; and the cure for those who have a large stone is more gentle than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have already said in the division the methods of cutting into stones, and the extraction alongside medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	And I have said the difference between a stone that is inflamed like rain, and all the signs, and in what case a stone must be cut of a certain size;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	And in the bladder, and in the testicles
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	And I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder often causes vomiting, and this is a sign that it has burst from the bladder as much as in its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and it lets out gravel, and makes the patient groan with pain, and it makes him vomit many times, and then turns black;
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and from these vomiting attacks the foundations are loosened
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and is light the healing of the attacks until they are three years old, and is much grief in old age, and is as harmful in youth as in old age.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	and it is the easier cure for those who have the large stone than for those who have the small one.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the limbs, loosen and move away, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder; and it does not go up towards the belly again; then set it between your hands as it appears, and put your hands on the patient’s thighs, so that the bladder is completely slumped downwards; then inquire and touch within; if you feel the stone in the space, do it with speed and cut over the stone immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not bleed at the touch, if you suspect fat in the left hand, if the patient is an adult, or in the middle, if the patient is a young man with companions; then grasp it in its foundation and inquire about the stone; and when you feel it in your hand, if it is at the belly of the bladder; then press on your hand, and the stone will go out on its own or you will see it cut.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the patient by the arms, and loosen and move towards the south, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not come out through the high part again.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then make him sit between your hands, and his hands rest on his thighs, so that his bladder is completely descending downwards.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then draw and touch inwards;
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the bone out of place, if you hurry up and hold above the bone immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if it does not yield with the touch, take your left thumb and index finger and apply oil to it, if the patient is old, or your middle finger if the patient is young and robust;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	And hold the bone in its foundation and draw the bone, and when you feel it at your thumb, if the bladder is at the neck;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	Then press on your thumb, and the bone will come out naturally when you see it slip out.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the nails above, and with his left hand to grasp the skin which is below the nails in the part where the size is taken.
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then I hold the bladder covering it, so that it is like this shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And I enter between that which is between the nails and the foundation, not in the middle but at the cost of the left nail
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And be two on the stone, and two either adjoined or to the foundation, and the size will be done if it is wide because of pushing, and inside narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, do not make it too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	By chance the press if the two which are or the foundation, that it leap forward for work.
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	and the nails that are part of the bone or that are angled, and margins.
si est griés a issir;	if they are grasped to break
