et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is part which is swollen, resembling a gland, and rounded, from which there is discharge.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	Therefore, if there are angles and margins, make the size greater;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not slip, you must grasp with the nails that are like a file at the head, because it must tear the bone if it does not escape
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you hold it with a subtle curve at the head
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you do not succeed in managing it, if the wound is large and the bone is fractured, if the bone is cracked without splintering.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are more than one stone, grasp the largest at the belly of the bladder first, then hold above, and then extract the others afterwards if there are several.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, if there arises much blood from the wound of oil and water, then treat with the salve of Dijon and balsam, as long as it is sane.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things are said to happen to the patient:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or he dies, or the urine comes to a standstill because his thighs cannot support it.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but all this effort you put into pulling out, or tearing out, will cause you to have chills until you pull it out piece by piece;
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	and when you have completed your work, if you apply incense, aloe, and dragon’s blood, and hold it still, and put over it a moist bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the burn
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then restore the patient on his collar, and do not loosen the link until the third joint below.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is either a tube or passage of the bladder, and is fixed in place, and the urine cannot pass; if the doctor of this whom I have mentioned before tells you to enlarge it many times, we shall hear of the size for this treatment.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if blood clots come to the wound and corruptions, and swelling of blood in the bladder, and either hold back the urine, which is known in part as a dry urine without mixing with the urine.
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Then take out the clot from the wound, and drain that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and carry it away
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound of acute and easy and soft, and give the patient all the help you can, as long as he is sane;
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And know that all the times you cure him, that you bind the two stitches, and gather the medicines above the limb
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is in the bladder or the urethra, and is fixed in place, and the urine cannot pass;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the cure for this which I say above is not sufficient, and you must do it many times, you will hear of its size in this cure.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then I take a thread and tie it around the bladder neck at the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then I grasp the thread lightly, until it reaches the stone; and I turn the thread back and forth at the stone until I can see the stone from the other side; when the urine comes, then I press my hand on that which remains of the stone that is in the bladder
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is burst, and spurts out with the urine, and is seen by the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason, if you take a thread from the stone and another from below, and pass the bladder towards the stone between the two lines, then grasp the stone and pull it out, and loosen the thread, and massage the blood clot which is in the wound; and the doctor should continue treating until it is healed
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the base of the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder.
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	Then pull the thread gently until it comes out at the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and turn the thread around the stone until you can pierce the stone from the other side
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	When the urine comes out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is in the bladder.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If the urine is broken in many pieces, and spurts out with the urine, and is stained with blood, the patient is in pain.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	If you are unable to do this by any means, if in this case you feel the stone in the bladder and another below, then put the thumb of your hand on the stone between the second and third ribs, then grasp firmly and extract the stone, freeing the loop of the vein, and compress the bleeding that is in the wound
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heal it until it is whole.</start_of_turn>
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third method if it happens that by chance one cannot find a woman who knows this art of hands; and the fourth method if the woman's stone is more blunt than the man's, for in this case one can make a deeper cut, and there is great fear of it. And if it is necessary to do this, if one takes a little knowledge of this, and touches the navel with the thumb, and if one does not find it, one must not cast aside the subtle art; and one should present a dance well known among women, or a woman who knows a part of this art, and command her to do what one commands of her with the inquiry of the stone; and watch well if the woman is a virgin: for in this case one can push back her burden or foundation and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, if she constrains her navel, one must recommend that she hold her navel or with the patient, and command her to stretch out her left hand on the bladder.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	It is known that the stone is retained in women, and if it does not happen again, it is a good sign, and is protected by three things:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	one is that the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	And the second is that one cannot find a woman who truly knows herself, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third is that it is often impossible to find a woman who truly knows herself in this art of lovemaking;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	And the fourth is that if the woman’s seed is more profound than the man’s, because it can make a deeper size, and great pain it has. And if you need this, if you take a woman who truly knows herself, and prick her right away, and if you do not find it, then there is no woman of sense in this world
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And the fifth is that there is a great wisdom in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and she commands that she do what you command of her with the inquiry of the seed.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	And look well if the woman is a virgin.
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	therefore he must push forward his head or root and question the bone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if the truth be told, if he constrains her head from the back, and he recommends that she stretch her head or with the patient, and press her left hand on her belly
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	if she tells the truth, if he can make her move from the belly to the flank of the belly until she reaches the root of the thigh.
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	then touch in the root of the thigh find the middle of the bone, lying or it is hidden there, and feel the bone in that part
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	and do not move his head up or down, and let the size be small at first
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	Then hold the limb steady in its normal position, if you feel the bone is too close to the wound until the bone can rest firmly, and the wound that many times before has been:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	that is to say, small and large, blunt and pointed, long and rounded, and which have rained.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the chill of blood has subsided and the limb has bled, if you return to your work while the wound is still open, until the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	If it does not subside, put on a wet compress and hold it for an hour until the bleeding stops.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the bone is firm, and have the instruments that I told you about in the extraction of the arrow as a help in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	if it does not stop, and it is an artery that is cut, if you put powder on the limb and strain with bands and compresses, and do not attempt to move it again, and leave the bone alone, and only by chance will the patient die
puis cure la plaie.	Then treat the wound.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white mucus, which is as dense as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and never is it truly in the yolk of the egg, if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the seed between the white mucus that we have mentioned.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	At no time does blood come out like angry flames, as we have said, and open the wound; and do not touch any intestines as you go, and if you do, it is because of fear, and repair them all every hour; and whatever remains if it stays too long in this place, if you believe the wound or abscess, until the intestines come out; and this is caused by the extension of the sinew which is like an angry flame, as we have said, because it is stretched, then is softened and pulled down by the wound and opened; and it is cured if it is by cautery, as we have said before; and never by iron in this manner: and let the patient lie comfortably on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the fracture and pull it out wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew which is from below the leather that covers it, then take hold of the nail and pull it out from the wound that appears from the sinew; and press on the wound at the navel, then cut out the two nails that appear from the sinew on the head of the nail; and cut the head of the nail, and do not touch the sinew or stretch the toe or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the sinew of the intestines; then cure it with the wound remedy.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Moisture is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white pus, which is like coarse grains of sand that contain the seed;
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	It is called "syfac," and never is it properly in the seed if we take care that it is not otherwise injured
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	It is the skin of the grain between the white pus that we have mentioned
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	It has not yet come out
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if there is an abscess with a portion of the bone, and because of this people think that it is one and the same bone; and if the moisture is between the skin of the bones and the soft tissue, if one feels well; then when you see the color of the moisture, if you think that it extends throughout, as we have said before.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	Never does it come out from percussion on the grains, and this pus is of many colors
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is pale yellow, or without redness, or black, or pale blue, and such things occur more frequently
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	These are the signs of gangrene in this assembly, for if it is yellow or white as we have said, if the abscess is round like a ball, and it does not swell with the coions, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if the abscess is round with a part of the yolk, and because of this people think that it is another ball.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	And if the moisture is between the skin of the coions and the white surface, if it smells bad;
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	Then when you see that the color of the moisture is like this, if you sense all around that it is sour, in that case
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the urine corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then cut the limb throughout the suspension, drain the urine, and cure it as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	When we burn the edges with iron, if you believe that the patient is well according to the poor and the filling of his flesh;
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	Then the swine lies on its back, on something somewhat high, and puts under it a bundle of towels.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	Then it sits on its left side, and instructs the minister to sit on the right, and extends the limb towards the second rib of the two ribs closest to the ribs of the hips
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the sponge, and grasp the skin of the hips between the loin and the loin, and make a complete incision dividing the skin of the hips until white fat is seen, and brown it thoroughly until it turns pale green
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	Then pierce the bladder straight with a large opening, and drain all the urine, and then put in the sponges, and extend the bladder upwards
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	Do not touch the hip bones, but only the bladder slightly
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Cope all at once or in pieces by yourself the cost of it to him secretly, for if you do not cope it well wisely, it will return to you acute.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the blood spurts from your work towards your work, if you leave it in its place when you have finished the work with the knife;
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put together the two limbs of the shoulder at a joint, and then cure it as the others wounds until it is healed
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	and if you find the work corrupted by another disease, you must believe that you must bind the vessels that are suspended in doubt of the discharge of blood;
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	then cope the limb at all the suspension, and extract the blood, and cure it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if it is acute and assembled in two parts together, its stakes are two branches.
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	if you hold the other part as you did the first equally, then dry the wound and put in the wound a cloth soaked in rose oil
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put another cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, and put on the two nails, and put on double layers of cloth, and bind it up according to this shape:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths and use coarse wool like this shape and join them with stitching in the armpit, and one of the nails grasps on the foundation up to the shoulder, and the other on the painful part
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two nails on the two angles, and be everything assembled together the restriction in the armpit circle
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And never is medicine this cautery branch like the size of iron; take instead a cautery cultellaire subtle, and prick the skin of the joints, and if necessary eschew as we have said, so that the white substance which contains the poison is discovered.
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	If you take the cautery as we have said, and prick that membrane as we have shown, and burn with this subtle cautery,
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	And prick in every way that you can, until you have scraped all of it off.
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	And keep that the fire does not touch the egg;
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	And burn until this egg is more scabbed over
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And watch carefully that blood does not flow, and that the work is done skillfully.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	If nothing else hinders you, or an abscess bursts or blood flows, or any other mishap, if you can, cure what hinders you, according to what is said above.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	If the patient is pale and hesitant, and does not wish to undergo this work because of its horror, if you deem it necessary, as I have said, and when you are certain by the indications that the wound has healed, if you wish, you can set the patient down in a raised position.
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	Then pierce the abscess at the lower part with the entire width of the palm of your hand, and make the perforation deep enough to reach the bone;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	And let the opening be large enough that all the pus comes out cleanly
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	Then put a swab on the wound, and bind it, and leave it open to drain the remaining fluid, then cure it until the wound is healed
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	If the wound does not drain pus from its opening, it is necessary to drink a dose of the instrument used for treating hydrophobia, for in this way it will form as before.
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the wound does not drain pus from its opening, and the infection recurs, it should be opened again after six months or when convenient, and when it is closed as before, the patient will be cured of his ailment.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on a high seat, then support the suspension of the collar bones from behind his shoulders, around all the vessels that are protruding from the hip, and grasp them firmly, and stretch them out; then cut with a sharp knife wide through where the vessels are broken, until they are uncovered, and then draw back the clot from the root, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle or there is a double thread, and tie it to the first root or where the vein has come from, and tie it loosely to the other root; then cut around them evenly, according to the length of the bone, and draw out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as usual or we plaster it, so that no vessel is cut except for those that rise from the collar bones; for by this means there will be no harm, and if all the vessels rise up, it is enough to draw out the collar bones to all the vessels; if so, they will not lose their nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and will dry and will not be aided.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	When the section of this limb has doubt or fear of more serious complications, I believe it is better to leave it as it is
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I will tell you about the work and the symptoms of an abscess
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	Therefore, if an abscess comes or bursts, and if there are boils;
et c’est par mout de cas.	And thus it is by experience.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by experience that it is painful and harmful to stretch things too much, as in the case of wounds or percussion;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the wound is like the color of healthy flesh
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	it does not feel any pain, and is a wound of grief
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and by chance there is a bleeding wound, painful and bloody, with discoloration of the color, and never comes from a vein or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is not from a vein, if it is known by the disposition of the wound to be hot, when you press it with your hand;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	it is only that you should touch it lightly
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	Whoever is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of pain in the two hands, and can well make the size of this semblance, and of the others.
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Whoever is made of the swelling of a vein is known by his disposition at the expression of pain in the two hands, and can well make the size of this semblance, and of the others. And it is that you must keep the head of the bone upwards, and the body of the bone white with fat, and deliver the ligament from all parts of the bone.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the bone is already softened with these bones, if you must then draw the bone, and keep it fixed;
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is hollow with the fat, or in what is in the blood vessels, if you must draw it out, and keep it rounded
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the buttocks.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering resembling a berry, with the softening of the hairs, and the patient groans greatly when he moves; and the cure for this disease is well known as much as this one that we have just mentioned, and all the learned men will tell you the work of this is as perilous as this one.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit on a high seat, then support the suspension of the collar bones from behind his shoulders, around all the vessels that are protruding from the hip, and grasp them firmly, and stretch them out; then cut with a sharp knife wide through where the vessels are broken, until they are uncovered, and then draw back the clot from the root, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries in the temples; then insert a needle or there is a double thread, and tie it to the first root or where the vein has come from, and tie it loosely to the other root; then cut around them evenly, according to the length of the bone, and draw out the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as usual or we plaster it, so that no vessel is cut except for those that rise from the collar bones; for by this means there will be no harm, and if all the vessels rise up, it is enough to draw out the collar bones to all the vessels; if so, they will not lose their nourishment from the incision of the vessels, and will dry and will not be aided.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess enclosed by a covering resembling an eyelid, with softening of the surrounding tissue, and the patient groans in pain when he moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	The treatment for this ailment is indeed as perilous as the former one, and all of you should know the work of this chapter, as the ancients have done.</start_of_turn>

puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	Then if he thrusts in a needle or if there is double thread, and binds it to the first bone or the head of the nail has come loose, and binds it to the other head.

Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The events of this branch are by incision coming from the navel or from the swelling above the belly in the groin, for the intestines descend from that passage to one of the buttocks.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this passage is either by incision from the navel or from the swelling of the groin, and comes from two ways:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or by percussion, or by jumping, or by pressure, or by the elevation of pain below the belly, and by similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the sign that it is by swelling of the navel is that there is swelling and swelling in a long line, and does not come immediately
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and is the swelling equal until towards the navel, because the navel presses the intestines
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient must retain the intestine in its place in the wound, if it can enter; then either tie a knot on its collar between your hands, and hold the thighs; then turn the thumb upwards, and grasp all the skin of the buttocks long; then take hold of the intestines from the belly button to the groin; and as much as you have seen to open the wound, and do as much as you can; then uncover the section of the intestine that is under the skin of the buttocks, until the fatty section is discovered throughout; then put your index finger into the hole that is between the fatty section which is under the skin of the buttocks, and the second section, and withdraw that which is behind the belly button, and between the second section; and then move the thumb of the right hand into the hole of the buttocks, and place the fatty section at the top of your left hand, and keep the belly button against all the sections; and command the minister to extend the belly button upwards, and untie what is behind the knot; and ask at your sides if there is any intestine or fatty section that is hard, and if you find nothing, if the gut is in its place again; then take a needle or make a large thread of X threads, and pass it through the back part of the section, which is after the skin of the buttocks; after the belly button, then grasp the threads that appear from the needle, until there are three threads; and join them together in the shape of a cross, and tie the section, which we have said is under the skin of the buttocks, with a strong knot of two parts; then cover the threads with cloth, and tie them together in two parts, so that no vessels that support them can enter into the wound, except for the staple, which should not be too tight; and adjust the knot according to the first knot that you did two fingers from that; and after these two knots leave the section of the intestine that is under the thumb of the buttocks with a space of two fingers; and after all the rest according to the roundness of the belly button; then grasp the part that is under the skin of the buttocks, until it is without tension, and bow as we have said before; then apply coarse wool soaked in oil, and put it in the wound, and apply the knot that we have said.

For in this work, it often happens that blood flows out due to opening a vein; and if it is delayed at the root, if it is raised with warm water, put on what has been said above until it flows; then treat the wound with another remedy, until it is completely healed.

Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	At no time does blood come out like angry flames, as we have said, and open the wound; and do not touch any intestines as you go, and if you do, it is because of fear, and repair them all every hour; and whatever remains if it stays too long in this place, if you believe the wound or abscess, until the intestines come out; and this is caused by the extension of the sinew which is like an angry flame, as we have said, because it is stretched, then is softened and pulled down by the wound and opened; and it is cured if it is by cautery, as we have said before; and never by iron in this manner: and let the patient lie comfortably on his back between your hands, then grasp the limb of the fracture and pull it out wide according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew which is from below the leather that covers it, then take hold of the nail and pull it out from the wound that appears from the sinew; and press on the wound at the navel, then cut out the two nails that appear from the sinew on the head of the nail; and cut the head of the nail, and do not touch the sinew or stretch the toe or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the sinew of the intestines; then cure it with the wound remedy.

dou chastrement	Dou chastrement.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	Wounds that are caused by sharp objects is forbidden in our law, and because of this I do not wish to speak of them in this book.

puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Then cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure. Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are tears in veins which do not usually heal without treatment; and when they are old they become black. We have already mentioned the signs and symptoms of such ailments, and I will now tell you of those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and blackheads, when pressed into the marrow, are not felt, except by the physician. It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the blackhead and press it into its roots, then sprinkle on medicines which restrain blood, such as alum and dragons blood and incense, and the like; then leave it for an hour, then put it in cold water; and if there is still blood, let her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and the like, then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and cheese, and make a plaster of it. And if it swells, that is good. If not, make her vomit at the back and give her vinegar with wine vinegar, and make her vomit. And when the abscess rests, if it has cured the limb of its swelling as long as it is sane; and the one which is called "albathir" is red, and is like a rough beard, if you cover it as I have said the blackhead. And then it will heal as long as it is sane. et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the wound remains clean and healthy.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce, but let me make the patient groan until the pain has subsided; then have the patient sit on a chair and put two cushions under his feet, and support his back and join his limbs together so that his thighs are spread out and his knees are resting on the bed; then draw up the dressing towards his chest and bring the instrument which we use to open the belly of the mare, so that it comes out in its natural form; and know that when you bring the instrument close to the belly, check the depth of the wound so that what enters through the instrument does not go deeper than necessary and does not damage the patient; and if the instrument is too large, cover the depth of the wound with cloths so that the instrument does not cause pain; and know that you must put the horn of the instrument at the bottom and hold the instrument.

I can teach you to restore the limb: if it cannot be restored, if you make the woman rise up, cry out; if she cannot cry out, make her groan on her tongue, and extend her legs forward; then bring in the muscle I mentioned before; and if she does not cry out, make her sit on the seat, and observe to restore the limb; and when the limb is restored naturally, make her cough, and command her to hold still until the child is gone.

et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman of a dead child or an empty womb, if she does not come to her senses, and you are constrained by the work of your hands; if you suspect that the woman is of sound mind, and has no accident or fears of death; Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine;	And if it remains after this treatment, and there is no more pain, as it is commanded by the dance, that she moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in alum, and then lay it in its place, and do the same with the other hand

Many children are born who do not have a firm basis of understanding, and as soon as they are grasped, they are struck with a subtle stupidity: if you can therefore command the dance that she breaks that stupidity at its root, and do not prick her with any harsh punishment, and keep the dressing that she does not touch; then put on a soft cloth in wine and oil, and the cure of oil until it is healed
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is like seeing a dog, and one puts on the head in the middle, and the large head above the fire;

Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have the true foundation perceived, as they have been stifled by a subtle fever

Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistules that arise from below the foundation are nodules, and those that arise from above the foundation deviate, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or several; and when the nodulation is old, if the swelling persists, and is accompanied by moisture, mucus or blood, these fistulas never cease; and they are known by the patient when he makes an evacuation, or by the escape of gas.

And thus one knows the permanent fistula at the foundation, and not the passing kind: if you bite your thumb or index finger at the foundation and insert a thin needle or piece of iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that arise from the root are nodulation, and blisters that arise from below the root are called deviation, or in the space of two parts, if there is one fistula or several

If the patient feels pain in the root of the limb, if you must bite your thumb, if you sense that the attempt has been perceived; or uncover or sense between your thumb the marrow or the bone, then take away that which is superfluous; for if it does not yield, it will not be healed

Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery, two things are assembled: namely, the burning of these hairy joints, and the incision of blood and the drying of moisture; then comes the treatment of soft bands bound firmly with thread or in pieces broken in half, as long as the bones groan and sweat; and it is best to leave the burnt hair in the wound; then treat the wound of the abscesses with dry sponges.

Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For the fire cautery consists of two bones together

des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer. dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when it is dry of fire or foundation
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	Wounds are of two kinds:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	Or else they are deep within the foundation, like grains of resin; and there are some that are small and some that are large, and in their course there is blood, and there is one or more of them, and they break through the foundation and the head of the foundation.
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	But those that break through have much moisture, and are accompanied by blood, or a drop of citrine urine, or blood, and are of a yellow color
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the cure for those who are within the foundation is that you command the patient to stretch out and rise to the chamber, as long as the foundations are forced out, and the nails are seen;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you are in a hurry, and you hold them with nails, or you hold them with your finger, then break them off at their roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	If the shoulder blade is not held by its moisture, if you take it with a drape, or a bandage, or a piece of chamlet;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	if you pull it out, then hold it, and sprinkle upon it warm powders that will take the place of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you burn them if it is said or as the master of cautery directs, for the other cures are not as effective as when it is healthy
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	if the foundations cannot withstand it, if you bite the patient with a biting and rough plaster to uncover what is beneath, so that it can be healed openly
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	cannot the patient bear it, and if the thread is strong enough to reach the foundation, if the cure is slight;
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And it is that you grasp them at your nail or with tweezers, and you pull, then you cure as we have said, until it is healed, and that you fear the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	If it is known that you can restore the limb according to this method:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	I take a thread whole, and I pass it through a needle, and then I pass the thread under and make the needle pierce through the other side, and I twist two threads of the thread beside the needle, and if it is thick;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and I tighten the thread firmly, then I knot the thread, and I pull out the needle, and I make sure that all the other threads are secure; and I leave one to correct the excess blood
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then I put on the foundation a soft bandage soaked in rose oil or beeswax, and put on the foundation, and command the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave it [hair] until it sprouts, and when it has sprouted, if the cure for itching and other cures are applied, while he is still sane.
dou fremit	immediately.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small, prickly growth that appears before a boil, and goes out with much pain; and never does it cease to irritate, and it is felt as though dead from pain, and comes throughout the body, and there is no part that is not affected by it.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you can keep it at the point of a hair or at the nail’s edge, the crust that is under it will not leave it moist.</start_of_turn>
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then leave the cure until it is healed if it can be kept.</start_of_turn>
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if it cannot be healed, if you must repeat the shaving more strongly than before, while it is still moist, and be scraped off.</start_of_turn
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then leave the cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if thou seest, if thou do this of a wasp or of iron in this fashion, and be silent and restrain thy hands:
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formice is a small outgrowth that appears before the bone, and goes out like a thorn.</start_of_turn
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And never did I see the true form of fear, when it sits so still like death, and comes into the whole body, and more than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And if you take a goose quill or a strong vulture quill, and put that quill on the fear, as long as the circles of the fear swell the fear all around;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand all the way around until you embrace the fear all around, and press it down firmly, and pull the fear out by its roots.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and be silent and restrain thy hands, do not perceive, for it must hold still, and press and if thou seest, if thou cauterize the edge, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	I do not know, for I am holding two things at once, and I am pressing both.

Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let neither the medicine be too hot nor too cold; smear the chief with ointment of oil or balm of eggs, or something like that; then bind it loosely; then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is quite visible; then draw out the ointment, and leave the patient his legs exposed, and if the medicine sees that it is sufficient, if the swelling has subsided; and if he sleeps a whole night, that is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he limps with a disease of swelling of the belly, and the physician hasten to leave, if he returns as long as he is well.</start_of_turn>
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and if there is a suspicion or the belly is tied, if you see it, and if you pierce it from the outside or from the inside

Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	Neither too hot nor too cold should the medicine be; oil or egg yolk, or something similar, should be added to the tip of the clip, and it should be bound lightly

Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned the treatment of wounds in the previous section; or you may say the treatment of hands and medicine, according to their completion.

Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things which are made for wounds are done with the bite of a stone, and the size of a spear or nail, or an arrow or a tube or a file, or similar things; or that are made according to the rules of surgery, as for wounds that bite on the neck, or on the head, or the arm, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for a simple wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head alone, for the memory will come to mind in its chapter.

If the wounds are deep and swollen, with much pus, if the wound is pierced or lower down the limb; if the artery is severed, blood flows freely; if the bone is fractured, the marrow and the cautery mingle; if the wisdom tooth is pierced, or the cheek, and the tongue is held, because the meat hangs there; and then tighten the wound gradually, and leave it alone for a while, then cure it with ointment until it is healed; if the wound has made an impression in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments are numerous, do not attempt to remove them all; leave as many as possible, and let the wound heal naturally; and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with powder as I have said.

And when it is cold, soak the area slightly: moisten a sponge or lay a wet cloth on it only, or pour on in boiling water squinching and scraping, and draw out the intestine as much as the swelling allows; and never do this without first restraining it, for it is useless to do so when the swelling has subsided.</start_of_turn>

ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	either by the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the fruit.

et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and do not make this wound strained, and be still that we may see how it swells.

et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, if there is a wound in the instrument with which one grasps the haemorrhoids, it is to be coped with the wound open.</start_of_turn>
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to make it immobile that the size, that one must not cut excessively without great necessity.</start_of_turn

I will return the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound will be closed after fifteen days. The cure was successful and the patient recovered.

et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And thus it is necessary to apply what I have said in great and moist wounds.

et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	This is the common method of stitching, and you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the wound’s size, then leave the head of the wound free for a space, and pierce a needle or there is good strong thread;
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	And pierce the two shoulders with the two thumbs, which is to say to split the skin from the inside, as much as you make the pierce from that part, and reunite the two thumbs with the three fingers together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then strain a double thread around the needle of two parts, then reunite the two thumbs of the wound following, and then leave one space, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then bind the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing so until you have made as many needles as you have seen necessary, until the wound is completely restrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And let the needles be neither too thick nor too thin, because the thin needles will tear all the flesh, and the thick ones will not penetrate properly
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	For this reason it is advised that they be blunt.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and it is not advised to push the needles too far beyond the hair and skin, as they may tear and open the wound before the suture is complete.

et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this method of stitching with needles is more manageable in small wounds, because there is a needle or two left over.</start_of_turn>
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second suture is common, and is that you join the two edges of the skin and the two edges of the tissue together with a needle or with one strong middle thread.</start_of_turn
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have perceived these things altogether, if you rejoin the needle at the part where you began, in the manner in which you cut the threads.

This stitching will secure the home, and I sew a wound where there was a wound before, which was caused by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm of great, and there were intestines well two palms of great, and the wound was in the belly.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does with great care, if it is done without violence, which joins the two parts naturally, and brings one chief close to the other chief, in this manner: pierce with a needle or the chief of a nearby splinter, and pierce only the lower part, and leave the two chiefs of the splinter; then withdraw the needle, and pierce from the lower part until it reaches the centre, having two chiefs of the splinter; then pierce one and the other from the lower part until it reaches the centre, in two other splinters which are on the other side; and this is the wisest method of stitching and the most common.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the blood had been vomiting that he would die, and this was a miracle;

Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Or you may say the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and pass it from the underside up to the underside again;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	When it has pierced the mark straight, if the thread slips or breaks or you have passed the needle, and you must pierce again from the underside of the part downwards until it reaches the underside
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And the understanding of this stitching is that you sew just as the leatherworker does the skin, and that you leave once the hair of a side, and you take hold of the other side, until the stitching is complete
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does very well, is if there is no break in the substance of the tissue, which naturally joins the two parts together, and joins one of the chiefs to the other chief in a partial manner.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Stitch with a needle or chief from the neighbouring part, and pierce only the latter, and leave the two chiefs of the tissue;

Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or I must tell you the cure for fistula, which is made by the work of the hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that arise in all members with pain; for there are wounds that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the jaw, or the intestine, or the bladder, or at some of the bones, or at the spinous process of the back, or at any joint of the hands or feet; and if part comes to the property of the main limb, and the rest.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	A fistula is according to truth a nodulation that must be firm and white, or there is no pain, and it is as strong as the quill of a bird
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	It sometimes appears clear and sometimes thick;

c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of the blood or bone
ou por sa malice;	or by its wickedness; ou par la brûlure de feu; ou par la violence de la plaie; ou par le mouvement des os; ou par la mors du sang; ou par le mouvement des fibres; ou par la dessication du corps.

ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	Or because the corruption is like the cause of pestilence.
