et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already mentioned these causes, signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or major arteries are not obstructed, neither the bones nor the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is broken, and there is corruption and blackness, if the marrow is whole as long as the corruption is of bone only, then heal the fractured bones with warming compresses until they are healed; and if they are not healed, bend them as before, extract the bone fragments until they are gone; if the fracture is complete, and when it is completely healed, restore the limb to its original position.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Sores that form in all limbs with pain in the bone
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	because there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the bone, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spin of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	If part of the limb comes to the property of the main limb, and there are similar symptoms.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are of this kind are of great suffering and healing, and there is nothing but toil and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	And if there is no fistula that does not come out only as I have said, and you have promised healing, and you see it proceeding, if you take an attempt to drain or cauterize, if the fistula is straight, if not;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	And if the fistula is tortuous, if a subtle attempt to drain it causes the swelling to rise around the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	And if the fistula has holes and you do not manage it well with attempts, if you listerize it through one of the holes, because moisture is short from one hole to another, and it swells up.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	Then when the shoulder joint is grasped firmly, you must know if there is a bone or nerve involved, and the limb is firmly bent inwards; ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and where exactly.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	And when you truly know where it is, if it is far from the joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any other bones that I have mentioned, if the limb can be repositioned as I have said, then force the fracture and the corrupted humors that are inside
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Then leave it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well formed, if you can reposition the limb as you wish, then put gentle pressure with medicine, and keep it tight until the medicine dissolves the surplus that is left at the bottom
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then I put on gloves of silk, so that they are clean;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if they are not clean by this, if I cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by fistula, if I grasp it.</start_of_turn>
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If the vein or nerve does not give you pain or the principal limbs, as we have said.</start_of_turn
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, if the limb remains as long as the corruption is all bony, then I will treat it with the aforementioned silk gloves until it is clean.</start_of_turn
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	And if they are not clean, and return as before, I will say that you are not going away until you are clean.</start_of_turn
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	If you discover and desire as much as you are at the bottom, and break all corruption, then restore the limb.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is now sound, that is good.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, say that the corruption is too great, that you will not be able to do anything about it.</start_of_turn
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature.</start_of_turn
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small bone that is corrupted, and you attempt to remove it with forceps, if the extraction is done with a suitable instrument and if there is any remaining bone, do not leave it behind.</start_of_turn
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture opposes you, and there is no risk or fear, if you grasp and hold moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you do not restrain them at an hour, if you put something above the wound that engenders corruption, and leave them as long as the wounds are raw around the bones, then they will have less pain in the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	If it is a large bone, such as an arm or leg, if you leave the corruption so long as the marrow is entirely ossified, then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	And if there is a great part of corruption, and it comes up to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then you must cover it and cover all until the corruption is gone, and then cure it until it is healed
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And I will tell you of a fistula that happened to a woman in her leg, so that you can take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	He was once a young man of thirty years, who had a pain in his leg from a cause within the body, as the things came to the leg, and fled from a great abscess, and had no other cause to fear by opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but he remained mad from his folly to open as much as the abscesses, and in corrupting much matter, and became fistula, and there came forth much pus that all the bones and moisture of the body were given over.</start_of_turn>
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and remained mad for two years, and there was no sense in the art of healing, as far as I remember, and went away from his leg and the medicines which they were using, and what was causing it through the pus at great pain.</start_of_turn
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and his skin became red like blood, and had the color of citrine.</start_of_turn>
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no part of the limb, if you must bind it in this manner: take one thread and stretch it at the head of the bone which breaks, and command no one to lengthen it upwards; and put another thread of linen thicker than the first one on the other side of the bone, and bind it over the scale which is detached from the bone, and stretch the head, so that you tear the corrupt scale away from the bone, and uncover the scale on the limb or where you see it is bound; and put a cushion or a piece of gauze under the bone to cover the corrupt scale, and bind as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bind once more.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I have done the same, and I found in one of the holes as much as I could uncover a part of the bone, which I found corrupted and putrefying, and it went as far as the marrow inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw that which appeared to me from the bone corrupted, and I thought that there was no other corruption except that which I saw;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with various medicines, so that it should not fester
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I repeated it, and I found the bone just as before, and I saw the corruption continuing in the bone, and I cured it, and then I left it, and I worried about restoring the limb
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could only do that until I found a palm of the bone, and I was forced to take it out completely, and I restored it with medicines
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And he became sane and joyful again, and did not wish to continue the work for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for fear of death which I avoided for him.
dou feu	fire
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if his bone is broken in any limb, if you can bear in this manner:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	I take it [the limb] and strain it at the head of the bone that breaks, and command that no one extends it further up
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another layer of linen more thick than the first layer, and tie it on the flesh that comes out of the bone, and stretch the head, so that if you pull the corrupt flesh away, you uncover the bone above the limb or where you see it is being bound, so that the hair does not stain the linen;
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And put I a sponge or a ball of toweling soaked in oil over the bone to cover the corrupted flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And cover so well as we can see and feel the corruption, and cover again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, if you uncover the flesh entirely;
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then put I a sponge soaked in oil, and then cover from one side to the other the corruption, and be the sponge long as the corruption itself as we have said
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint, and cover the bone or what it contains on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, if there is no other vessel but to cover it.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the corruption is from the hand or from the foot, if it is strong in that matter, but all the same you must inquire about that corruption, how it appeared to you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And keep the body in all ways that you can, but that the vein or nerve does not hinder you
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And the nails that are cut into the bones are many, according to the size of the bones and the appearance of swellings, and their thickness and thinness, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And for this reason it is necessary to appear suspicious of the work of the instrument
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the nails that the work will show you the instrument from which you will be in need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manner of diseases
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you ponder the instrument which you must employ according to this, it is certain.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the limb too much, or if you put on restrictive powders; then return to your medicine until it is accompanied by something; then bind the limb securely with a strong bandage, and treat until it is healed; and I will tell you that in this house there was a man with a black spot that seemed to burn, and that corrosion began in his palm, as it burst all the bones; and when we saw the corrosion, if we did not cover the bone, he was healed; and long after the corrosion had gone, the palm returned, and it came to me, and I put on protective things after the inflammation of the sore, and I could not stop the corrosion; and I advised him to cut off his hand, and I did not want to give him any hope of recovering the matter; and I doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die, for the strength of the body was weak; and he awoke, and returned to his home, and he covered his hand, and he was healed; and I have never heard of anything like it except for this, when we have been forced to do it.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder may be dislocated due to moisture, or by tension, or by violence;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	When you have treated the inflammation with medicine, but it does not help, if you can cover that limb up to the root of the dislocation or if the inflammation comes back, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by malice, which is greater, from the defect of the limb
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and afterwards comes the blackness, for that inflammation of the limb consumes the limb piece by piece, and takes hold of the whole body
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you hurry to cover it up, and if there are venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and the like, if the inflammation is at the top of the arm, if you can cope with it, and do not give it space to come down to the hand
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if the nail has slipped from the joint, so that the cortex does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if it comes up to the arm, if the nail has slipped from the cuticle;
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes the cuticle, that is death, and nothing but the quantity of its force is of any avail.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus do all the things when the cortex comes or the bone is affected.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, if the nail follows the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes with the bone, if the nail grasps all the bone
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it reaches the forearm, if the nail has slipped from the joint of the elbow
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes from below the knee, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And if it comes from below the knee, if there is no other remedy but to leave the patient to die; then grasp the limb with a cloth or bandage and stretch out one finger of the lower limb and another finger of the upper limb, and divide the flesh between the two fingers at a one-inch interval, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then grasp the limb with a cloth or bandage, and put a cushion under the drape of linen, so that the bandage does not touch the sound limb, and cause the patient other injury and incision
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if blood comes out when you work, if you cauterize the limb urgently, or put on some restraining powders;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the limb securely with a strong ligature, and cure it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you that there is often at home in summer:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	there was a black bile that seemed to burn like fire, and that corruption came first in its belly towards the heel, as it burned all the flesh
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	when the host saw the corruption, if he covered the flesh and it healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and long after it returned the corruption or the heel of the foot, and he came to me, and I put things that would impede the corruption after the purification of the wound; but the corruption did not cease
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he told me that I should cut off the limb, and I did not wish to give him any hope of recovering the matter
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	And I doubt that if I cut off his hand, he will die, for the strength of the man is weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And he awoke suddenly, returned to his land, covered his hand with a cloth, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	I only heard of this story because of what we are about to do
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Blood often comes out in the course of a vein, and it lingers for such a long time that it makes a great swelling
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then it runs back and breaks, and the blood spurts out, and swells up the veins like vessels
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	The skin that is under is as thin as a bandage, and does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain" and not "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	But if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone under the skin, it is called a fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the wound if it is closed with such force that it tears the skin around, and even when it is subtle, like a drape.</start_of_turn>
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal by itself.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have sewn that the skin is healed, and the corruption is not in the depth, and the skin is thick like leather, then the treatment of the fistula is as follows:</start_of_turn
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	look if there is pus, and if it has a foul odor, then apply Egyptian medicine plaster which is made.</start_of_turn
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take alum, oil, and beeswax, equally, and mix the wound with these ingredients in a vessel over the fire until the medicine is red and as thick as honey.</start_of_turn
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	And then take according to your need, and make it acute and mellow, and in clinking the belly, and restrain the part.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	And leave the medicine in place for two hours, then remove it while expressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Do this several times, until the belly is soft and the pain is gone
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Never clench with acute water, when this medicine is not present; take wine of must, vomit, and discharge, then clench until you are certain that the belly is well healed
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	If the patient cannot bear it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the water of vinegar, if you clench with water and honey or if there is a little bit of blood;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	Or you anoint it with honey and wine mixed together, for the honey has the property of softening and washing away, and the wine makes the wound dry.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And when you have done this, and you have secured that the wound is well softened, if you anoint it with what has been said to make new flesh appear, and take away the crust with oil of rose and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	Or you anoint it with some medicines and poultices, of which I have spoken of the properties or treat with poultices;
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And if the wound has opened in the flesh and the dressing will not enter, if it has been caused by a sharp object, put in a patch of Egyptian or basilon ointment until it is enlarged
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If the wound is too wide, if the edge and the skin leave too much slack, the clot or pus can enter; and if it bursts that the blood vessel is below, if the head or more downwards than it should be.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the blood vessel is pierced, if it does not leave the edge clean;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you do not cover the wound sufficiently as you see, if it appears in this manner: the blood vessel will run to the lowest point, because when the blood vessel is pierced, if it does not leave the edge clean, and if you do not cover the wound sufficiently as you see, if it appears in this manner:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	it runs lower down and does not leave anything of the blood vessel behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take solidifying medicines to put out the blood, and extend over the bandage of linen that covers all the wound.

et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And he who is outside the protrusion within often supports the socket, and pulls out the socket of that which is between the socket and the protruding part, if it is venom or blood or enough, or digested or indigestible.</start_of_turn>

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the incision of the abscess.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess which arises from the swelling of a pouch of the hand, or the foot, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is envious, and one does not take care, if it comes there will be a running abscess, and it will break and discharge pus until it reaches the root of the swelling, and by chance it will break all the way; and there comes the corruption up to the bone, so that there is sharp pain, and the head of the abscess is large, and the color is yellow.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are some who are late in their eating and drinking in their wounds, and those who do the opposite
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if they eat indigestively, salt remains in their stomach after a meal; the saliva does not flow properly

Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound, and the swelling is soft; and if the swelling is pressing on the nerve, and it begins to swell, and to bleed, if you must, put on the root of the swelling the right amount of cautery to stop the bleeding, and the pus that is above, and gently cut away that part of the swelling that is superfluous, and put on the remaining part of the swelling medicines that are astringent and corrosive to destroy all that remains; then let the wound heal until it is healed.</start_of_turn>

des vils	Des vils

Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment for fire is in two ways: one is with vinegar, and one must force out the black blood; or the other method is that you cauterize the vein, and you must force out all the blood.</start_of_turn>
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large vessels covered with thick phlegmas containing black bile, which come in abundance with many diseases of the limbs.</start_of_turn
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often appear in those who go to bed and work and travel, than in others.</start_of_turn>
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The ailments of the limb are thus: open the limb of the patient, if there be hair, then put or bathe it in hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you have no bath, if the patient is able to bear the heat of the fire, then burn the hair at the root of the limb, or in the part below the ankle; then cover the skin with ointment, and press the limb from the ankle downwards until it feels relaxed; and you will see it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white thread; then remove the hair from below, until it is freed from the skin, and then apply ointment lightly, and press it in another place nearby; then burn another size, or several if necessary, and when you have finished, remove the hair from the root and draw it out, until it is all gone; and if you do not manage to draw it out and it remains firmly embedded, then there is a splinter at the end of the hair, and you must grasp and draw it out, and there will be blood at the root, and wipe your hand with a part and with the other, until it is gone; and keep it still, for if you move it, you will not be able to draw it out or lift it, and this will cause harm to the patient; and when you have finished, put out the limb of the wound with clean wool and oil of roses and cure it until it is healed.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The fire cautery is as follows: instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the opening is made, if you suspect that the surrounding area is too soft, surround with a piece of sponge from one and a half inches to two and a half inches thick, and hold in place, and leave the sponge in the limb until it is all the way out; for if you pull out the sponge, if it enters the flesh, it brings about an abscess or gangrene or death. Therefore it is necessary that it be treated promptly and thoroughly from the very beginning, and that nothing be left or remain within; for I have known of cases where this vein has been treated with five palms of sponge, or ten, and one hon has come out to me from ten palms of length, and when it was pulled out, there was one wound or hole in the flesh, and all was lost.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein lies in the limb, in hot parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in the earth where there is no moisture.</start_of_turn

de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	When you see it cured and treated, if you cannot force it out, then do this: bind the limb above and below with a strong ligature, then press above and push down firmly; and if it does not come out, if you cauterize the fire above, until it dies; and the greater harm it does is if it runs into the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the oil, tear out its hair above, then press above and push down; and you must use the patient of the application of solid medicines for the bad humors carried, and give him nourishing food.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "bullous disease", for it often happens after boils, and is a small wound which originates between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, ascending and descending, and the patient feels it quite acutely from limb to limb, as long as the skin is stretched or when it is pulled, and even jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as veins, serums, bile, and worms or intestines
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and there is doubt about its malice, for when it runs through the body and ascends to the head, and comes to the navel, by chance it returns, and destroys the oil
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and treated, if one cannot force it except when it is going away:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it is certain, then bind up the limb above and below with a strong thread, and press upon it above and below, and if it does not move, if the fire cautery is applied above, until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest damage that it makes is when it bursts the oil, as we have said before.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	If you see it coming or near the oil, grasp the edge and press above, and pull downwards;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is proper to use the patient various applications of poultices and medicines that dissolve bad humors caused by dampness, and to feed him nourishing food that is not rotten.</start_of_turn>
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered how he managed to move about without wanting this sickness in this way.</start_of_turn>
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and is a pain that comes in spasms of the limbs, and because it moves from limb to limb.</start_of_turn>
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And I bear witness to that which I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	And I saw a woman who was sick, and I discovered a small swelling in her armpit;
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and I saw her arm rise up like a worm to her shoulder, more swollen than anything, as if there was gold inside when it struck the bone of the other side
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain went away from that limb and settled in the shoulder, and then a little while later it was corrected throughout the limb as far as the other arm
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that she often twisted her arm back towards the bone, as I saw her do it.
des saiettes	When you see the cure of this ailment, and the patient feels that pain, if it bursts like we have said, if the liquid above and below has become inflamed, then support above as much as that constraint of the liquid inside is strong; and cauterize the liquid; and if you do not see it at your eyes, if the cure for that which releases the constraints, like foul pills, and pills of serpin, and similar things.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	However, I do not wish to maintain that she was not experiencing pain in her limb, but I do not wish to lie, as I saw her do the same thing in the woman
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought that this was the cause of that woman's dry skin, uncovered veins, and that constrained windiness.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And I do not find that this is the reason for these things that are pleasant, and that have moist skin and veins that are full again.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	When you see that this illness is cured, and the patient feels this pain, if she tells you that when it happened previously, the windiness was intense, and then ceased as soon as that constrained windiness disappeared from her;
et cauterize le leu;	then cauterize the limb.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see that at your eyes, if he cures her of that which brings on the windiness, like foul pills, and pilules of serpin, and similar things.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it bleeds from none of these limbs, and the sign of death I will tell you later, know that if you delay the extraction of this arrow, death will follow in many ways; and when this sign appears, do not delay, for neither the arrow nor its wound will mend by itself.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	When the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces the bone, and blood spurts from the opening above the brain, this is when scraping and soiling and vomiting and shivering and redness of the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of senses, vomiting of bile; and by chance without a wound of the nose or ears; or by chance loss of speech and voice; and spurting of white moist blood resembling pus, and in spitting also like brown hair; and if this sign appears, if you delay treatment, take out the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.</start_of_turn>
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their points is such that some have great peaks, others have small, and some have ridges and sockets.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces of bone sticking out.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that break in no limb break in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the main bone cracks, as with the skull, forearm, shoulder, hip, ribs, intestines, bladder, and similar limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in no place of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, will teach you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	that you must beware of the extraction of this splinter, for death comes after in various positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this sign is absent, I do not perceive it; and the bandage is not mine in such a case. If the wound is treated, and the wound is cured.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the cerebrospinal fluid when it breaks and pierces the bone, and leaps up the blood which is above the brain, is when there is scraping, swelling, twisting, and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixing of the senses, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and sometimes without cause, or without noise;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes speech and voice are lost;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and leaps from the wound a white moisture resembling pus, and also like burnt hair.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign shows you, if you stay with the treatment, take out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it breaks or curves is that it is close to the left breast, and feels just as if it were fixed in something hard, do not fear; do not leave it empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	Sometimes the arrow moves like mice, and black blood flows without a wound, and comes cold sweat and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then there is doubt that the patient will die
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the sponge is split or the belly burst, and in leaping at any point of dung through the intestine root, if there is no hope of cure, do not attempt to extract the sponge.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	If the arrow breaks under the skin in the armpit, if it is not taken out immediately;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	it causes great pain and swelling and breathing difficulty
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And all the limbs move together.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	As for the other limb, if the face, the neck, the chest, the armpit, the groin, the shoulder, the elbow, the wrist, the hand, the foot, and the limb in general are affected by numerous disorders.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the sponge is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I have already told you, because of what you have done otherwise.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the bladder is split open and the urine spurts out and comes out forcefully, and the patient feels great pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	These wounds are mortal.</start_of_turn>
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in a game there was a sliver of wood that had penetrated the fat of the ear, below the cartilage, and the sliver was removed, and did not leave a mark except for the tip towards the heel, and the sliver was as large as a Turkish bow, and in all this time there was no damage to the ear; the game was healed, and there was no further complication
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take out an arrow from the throat of a Christian; and the arrow was Arabic: I soothed the barbs, and cunningly pulled it out until it was freed; and the Christian was healed.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	There is at home a wound where a hair or a tear is at the root of the nail:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I grasped it, and pulled it out from the other side of the grease of the ear, and it healed without any harm.</start_of_turn
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And I pulled out a hair from a game of hair that was in the grease of the oil from the marrow of the bone, and the hair was replaced, and did not reach anything except for the tip towards the ear, and the hair was as thick as a Turkish bowstring, all in all a very clear sense of hearing.</start_of_turn
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The just man was sound, and there came to him no evil occurrences.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And there went out a stone from the throat to a Christian, and the stone was Arabic to the ear.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I saw the beards, and I suspected until I went out, and the Christians were sound.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And there went out a stone from my home, that was in the belly or stomach, and I thought that it would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after XXX days, if it did not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut on the stone, and I grasped it, and I went out, and there came no evil occurrence.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if I went home where there was a stone that had fallen out or was behind, and there was a deep wound there;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And immediately take hold of the arrowhead within it, and do not change its natural disposition, do not find any hindrance in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And thus it is with another man, who had an arrow lodged in his face, and it was closed with a bandage.

et mout d’autres semblans.	and the like of other things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And thus drew an arrow at the king's palace, which was stuck in the middle of the nose, and was a weakening declension towards the lower part;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely recovered
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to the care after it had been stuck for three days
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I kept it for the days, and healed the wound completely, and reassured the patient for a long time, until he said that the splinter was no longer in his heel; and he told me.</start_of_turn
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I feel it at every moment, a slight tremor, and I do not feel it myself.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there is a tingling sensation and pain in the earlobe.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it might be an arrowhead. I put on a plaster dressing with a digestive agent, because of which the swellings do not increase
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the wound of the arrow appeared to me
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put on the plaster again, and I closed the wound properly, and I kept the patient calm for a long time, until the arrow was removed from his chest;
et il le me dist.	and he told me that it was gone
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put on an aqueous corrosive medicine on the wound by hand for a long time, until it was over, and I held it, and I felt the head of the arrow that remained in the flesh
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then I saw in the opening of the wound by that doctor’s hand, as the head of the arrow appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and passed through well the remainder of the three months, and then grew so wide that I was unable to close the wound, and I held it together with one hand and the other, and could not do anything about it.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	where I had to continue to struggle and devise ways to manage things, until I set the pins firmly in place, as it is written at the end of this chapter, until I had finished, and restored the wound
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians say that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or have you spoken of the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your cure on that which I do not say, for the books do not teach me everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But you know masters that I understand very well many great things, and that which is present and lacking, true nine works, and a new instrument, following the descending order of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out of members or are cut off for that matter, for two ways.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	Or by force or by other means;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which comes out by itself is an arrow that has penetrated flesh, and that must not be repeated any more.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the chariot is completely overturned, and rejoice at its coming out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, if you leave it for a few days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it will come out, and if it does not come out, if you force the chariot to turn completely over, until the wheels are splayed, and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the socket is stuck in the bone of the shoulder, and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some other ailments that I have mentioned to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if you do not treat it, but leave it alone until it is even again after some days, for if the socket reaches the scapula, that is death.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you do not manage it once, if the blood has clotted around the wound, then pull it out, for it is an alleviation.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if the abscess is firmly closed and will not open, if one administers tarres around it, as I have said;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then it will cure the abscess as long as it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	if the clot is placed back into the flesh if it cannot be seen, if one has tried everything.</start_of_turn
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, if the limb has no visible blemish;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you do not see the wound or the clot, and if there is no bone, nerve or vein, if the pain is great;.</start_of_turn
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	then pull out the clot if you see it, and if there is bone stuck in the flesh of two parts to the muscle that you pull, and then break or crush the clot’s ears until you can pull it out.</start_of_turn
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And be subtle, though you do not break the splinter, that you draw it out more firmly.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	Therefore take hold of it immediately, as long as the nails can grasp it, and then extract it: if it leaps out now.</start_of_turn>
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if blood flows out from the wound, contrary to what we have said about the treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	Beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and keep the wound closed as much as you can without causing harm, or too tightly or loosely, or firmly or gently;
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Put the patient in the position in which he was when the splinter slipped out, for that is the greatest aid, and if you do not know how, follow what your signs tell you
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The splinter comes from another place, or you see no opening, or the skin is stretched out in that place if you see it or feel it
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Tailes donc sur, tant que les tenailles puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai.
si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore take hold of the limb, as long as the nails can reach, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the dressing is torn or stained with blood or pus, and it is close by, grasp it firmly; if you grasp it, keep hold of the wound and the nerves, then extract it, and then sew the wound, if necessary; and cure until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot be moved, if you leave it in place, and then resume the extraction until it comes out again.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if there is a splinter of bone, it has burst open; hold it firmly at all times
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	When there is a break and you see that an instrument has pierced, if you administer it with a twist, so that the tip of the splinter enters the hole of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	Then extract it, and if the splinter is caught, hold the instrument at the point where the tip entered to make the extraction easier
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if it is known that the splinter is in the heel, the foot, the belly, the bladder, or the breastbone, and it is close, cover over it immediately if you can.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	cover the wound and the nerve, then extract it, and then close the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	leave it until it is healed.
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the teeth is such that they can bite and scratch if it is thus:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	There are many ways to do this.
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large or small, depending on the size of the splinter
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins that we must avoid in this place, which are 16 in number: two veins that are behind the ears, which are covered by fat; and two arteries that are in the two temples that appear; and two veins that are in the two armpits, which are covered by hair; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the base of the nose; and the two veins that are at the collar; and the two veins that are under the tongue.</start_of_turn
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins commonly known are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the breast, and they call it the great vein; the second is called the median, and is composed of the cephalic and brachial, and they call it the arm vein; and the brachial is either on the left or right side of the breast, and they call it the belly vein, and is above the collarbone, and is the one from which we draw, which often appears above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the ulnar and ring finger, and if there are two veins; and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is that which is below the curve of the left breast vein, and the second is the sole which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein which is called the sural, which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins like these.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	From veins where one has known themselves to be safe, there are either 16 or 17 of them, that is to say
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	two veins which are behind the ears, which are opposite the bones of the earlobe
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	And the two arteries which are in the two temples appear;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins which are in the two armpits of the two eyes, which are called “aspises”.
et li voine que est emmi le front;	And the vein that is under the forehead
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is at the back of the neck
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two strings which are in the ear or collarbone.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	And the two veins which are under the cheeks of the mouth, and these are the veins which are called “augeherich”.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	And two veins which are beside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly known are five in each arm.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic [dislocation], and is on the left side of the breastbone, and they call it the people "the vein of the head.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the minor [dislocation] is called "fast," and is composed of the cephalic and brachial veins, and they call it the people "the vein of the arm
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the brachial vein if it is on the left or right side of the breastbone, is called the people "the belly vein," and is above the rib cage, and is that from which we generally see blood leaking out openly on the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saving vein is the one which is between the elbow and the wrist, and if there are two rains.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	And in the arm and the forearm there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One of them, if it is on the left side of the rib cage, and the other on the right side of the ankle.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein which is called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other rib cage.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and on the other limb are three veins beside those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The blood from the veins which are behind the ears helps to expel old blood and evacuate;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the quality of the blood, as I told you, is that you raise the head of the patient and rub the hand or the veins are rough;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then stretch the patient's neck with a pin, until two veins appear behind the ears in two loops dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	When the thumb is stiff at your disposal, and if you feel a tingling sensation at the base of your thumb, take hold of it.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet and pierce through the vein until you reach the bone, then keep your hand firmly against the upper part of the vein, grasp and tear the skin and the vein well together, and let the blood flow until you see it
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then strain and tie it, until it is healed
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already mentioned incision and cautery or the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth an ancient pilgrimage, so much so that it causes swelling, nausea, and vomiting, and at the root of the tears there are pus-filled boils.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the same quality of health if it is like I have said.
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And that the patient is able to strain his neck, so that the two veins open widely.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the pulse below his arm, and then he raises himself up;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then keep the hand above your arm at your index finger, and hold the lancet below, and keep the vein above, and close the wound, as you have done with two other veins, and do as much to stop the bleeding as is necessary
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	Then loosen the patient, and put your hand on the vein for an hour, then put on a bandage
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And then leave it alone, and let it be until it is healed;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And thus we have spoken of it above and of their treatment and of their extraction, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The blood from the front vein is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein; it has diseases of the old face, and emigration, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	When the patient strains his neck by turning, as the vein bursts open.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument which is called the "forceps," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the point on the vein, and hold with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow out as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck, and bind the vein until it is whole and never again with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Whatever, it is not permitted to make the flames too great.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the same from below, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The blood of the two veins that are two palms wide if they aid the eyes, and the teeth, and the redness, and the yellow in the fat, and diseases of the face;
