Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then make the blood flow out steadily, as much as you are able, and then bind up, and bind firmly.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	When the blood in the vein is too thick, it turns to water, and causes swelling, boils, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and even when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	When the quality of the blood is that the patient bites his neck, then strain his arm at your left hand, and take a moderate flame long, and apply it to the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well enough, and it will not start to heal now
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	Do not go too quickly, and make the blood flow out steadily as you need, then bind up, because it is moist and will restore itself at night
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And thus is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	And thus is the form of the flame: the saliva from the two armpits helps to expand the spleen, to initiate fermentation, and to expel disease, and to cause hiccups, and to corrode, and to cause herpes, and to cause tumors.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the saliva is when the patient pulls out his tongue alternately from both sides, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Or the master is standing over the patient's head, and the patient sits on one seat, then open the vein widely, and take blood steadily, or as much as is necessary.</start_of_turn>

Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins which are below the tongue helps after the blood of the cephalic vein, and this is at the widening of the throat, and with eye diseases, and with mouth diseases; and the quality of the blood is that if the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and you touch the tongue, and look below each rib towards the costal margin of a black vein: close both of them, and do not move them too much, for below are the arteries.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And make him sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the face up, and look at the two veins, one on the right cheek and the other on the left, and know them by their blackness, and by the fact that there are small black veins running through them

So take both of them, and if you do not know them, and if you are in doubt, if the greater one is at the back, and also do the two veins which are below and above, because this is the right way

Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The blood of the veins which are below the tongue helps after the cephalic blood, and it is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth

Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins that we commonly call healthy are healthy in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or if they are pricked with a sharp flame like a burning candle, or olive oil as thick as trenchant earth, and is called "anesil".

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps to alleviate diseases such as hiccups, colds, hoarseness, pain in the side, and pain in the belly; and it is useful to know that it is linked to the artery which is opposite to it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And there is master in opening the large veins filled with obvious thick blood, which contains great blood and trouble;

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	And this is the form of the olive flame: the blood of the basaltic tree, which is one of these veins, helps with ailments such as sore throat, or swelling in the throat, or pain in the side, or belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the healer to know how to keep the blood steadily flowing, and that he beware of the artery which is close to it

eschui la donques.	Wash away the bloodstain.

et estainche li sans.	And he must hold it [the dislocated limb] still.

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The blood of the vein in the middle helps so that it heals without the head below and the bones below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the healer to be wary of the nerve which is below, and if it is not grasped firmly, and if he pulls it, it swells and the patient is either crippled or by chance cannot recover.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve often bursts, and if it does not burst in some home due to its subtlety, it is necessary to know that you must remove it with an instrument that is anesthetic

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is as you think

Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about health is that blood should only be drawn when absolutely necessary to preserve health and to ward off future diseases.</start_of_turn
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	or from the three veins that are in the wrist.</start_of_turn
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	namely the cephalic, facial, and basilar veins.</start_of_turn
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it must be done at the beginning of the meal with fasting and vomiting, and after eating when the sign of swelling appears.</start_of_turn
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And if one must strengthen the first joint or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing that is administered for ailments has no definite duration, but when it is necessary for a joint or nut, in all hours and at all times
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it must not be strengthened too much before twelve years, nor a woman who has borne for more than four months until the seventh month.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein bursts the first time, that is good; but if it bursts again, it must be stopped once and for all, or it will not be healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone sees that he is healed in any way, if it be possible, if there is a slight hernia, if there is retained phlegm, so that the veins do not swell the intestines with nourishing humors to the principal members
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	neither does one know that it is too sore from meat, nor that it is dry, as much as there is reason to be, neither hydrophiles
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if he suffers from vomiting, pain in the belly, and excessive urination in women, and travail, wakefulness, and slumber, and all the virtues, or by the weapon or poison;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtile the humors, if he is not already fat, by foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power to do so.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter or bathe, if nothing hinders you, to subtilize the blood, and to keep the pulse in the wrist or the side, as we have said
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep him busy with work, with anxiety, and with pleasures, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Bind him and comfort him, and keep the patient higher than the heel which we support, and wipe his hands twice or thrice, then gently pull the limb downwards, because if it is too tense or swollen, he cannot correct it without
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then he wipes the limb with his hands, until the veins swell, and one feels them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then he moistens the limb with a little oil, and places his left hand on that vein below the limb a palm or where he wants to see it healed, so that the vein does not bleed and cause damage.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flee just like strings to the healer, and if there are such that are filled with swelling, so that when the flame is put on, when it is taken away, it cannot open the vein, and this is what is to be feared.</start_of_turn
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it causes the vein to burst, if the wound is too wide, because of this one must advise the healer in these matters.</start_of_turn>
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If not, if it starts again immediately, take hold of the limb once more or hold it firmly in place, for if it has not burst.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	If the limb has burst, and the patient groans, if you leave it for one or two hours and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	surely there will be swelling.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it stops;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	if the wound is small, or if it seems that there is not much blood, do not doubt but that there is enough bleeding at the root of the wound itself
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And the work is often done hastily, even when the illness is severe.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for it often happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb inflamed, if you do not renew the blood flow, put on a little oil, for it softens the flesh of the blood, and makes it limp in this limb the oil that is on it
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in the wound to stop the bleeding of the veins; thus the blood flow is stopped
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and this itself brings about a tingling and swelling of the eye, when it is put on the limb;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if it is done carelessly and escapes when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, even if it does not burst except for this time or the opening of the vein is small, if you are hasty, put on the wet sponge immediately and over it a little charcoal, and hold for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And hold that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after a few days without any blackening or greening, if this does not trouble me.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see it, put nothing else on it of aloes or myrrh dissolved in vinegar, mustard, or the like.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times there comes an abscess and a discharge of blood from the basilisk.
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Put your hand upon it, and if you find the limb soft under the compression of the hand, that is an ominous sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Listen well that you do not place anything upon it of what we have said, for by chance in vain without an artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but it makes it swell dry to harden the limb, then treats it with another treatment, until it is healed
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him who has a cold constitution, it is to be given soft bread soaked in the juice of green apples; if he is faint, give him blood three times or four. And if he is of a cold complexion, mix before the blood soft bread soaked in beeswax, or in aromatic beeswax with spices, as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant oil.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is not black, if you leave it to fester as long as it is red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it large, if you leave it until it is subtle;
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hairy, if you leave it cold
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it must be known to him who is plain and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, that we make the wound larger and the flame wider;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the feeble-minded, do the opposite; make him safer thus, often and always, and must make him safer by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of bleeding is useful for stopping excessive bleeding and relieving pain, and is worth more than bleeding that lasts a long time without widening.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one who has a bruise, give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is pale, give him three or four spoonfuls of blood; if he is dark-complexioned, give him soft bread soaked in aromatic syrup of honey, or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant syrup
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself recover in another place, if he must recover on the second day or the third
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the body which is already clotted, and causes fever; if it is prudent to extract a great quantity, and to dilate the opening as much as it screams in pain; then that you reward all the blood conditions, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, that the blood does not reappear in place of the pain, and this often happens when the patient is negligent; and do not do so except when you see the limb slipping, and make the blood flow the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly; if it is crooked, that you extend the limb immediately, because that would be bad; but leave it as it is when it is well the second time; or you point at the tip of the flame, until the one which is frozen at the opening of the vein is forced out, and put on some oil and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has fled, if you leave it and do not restrain it, as long as the incision is calm.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood a second time, if the same vein is still bleeding, or in another vessel, or in the other arm.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood in the bruise that has already paled, and it causes fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If you are forced to manage a great quantity, and to widen the opening so that it hurts in the belly;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then you must restore all conditions of the blood, and put your hand over the pulse when it is sound, so that the blood does not come out in place of the marrow, and this happens often when the patient is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and do not attempt to move the limb a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly upon it
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if it is crooked, extend the limb as much as possible, because that would be bad
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but leave it until it is sound a second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you touch it with the tip of the flame, until the one that is frozen at the opening of the vein comes out, and put some oil on it and press lightly.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	If the patient grasps his hand in hot water, while the flesh is red; then bind it moderately, so that the wound opens well; and pull the limb through, neither too wide nor too long; or cut a large opening and draw the skin well up to the joint of the hand, and if it does not suffice, grasp the hand once more in hot water and leave the blood to clot in the wound, until you have enough; and if it is in this state, do not return the hand to the hot water, for more is put into it than in this; and the blood from this vein is more valuable than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the saliva of the right hand is valuable for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and immerse it in hot water, until the vein is emptied if we see it; and if it is pulled through, and if you press on it throughout, if it does not swell; and do not press too hard, for the nerves are all exposed without flesh, and then grasp the hand once more in hot water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and do not move it.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as well as you can, if you put oil and lint on the wound, it will help to heal quickly, and make a soft dressing.</start_of_turn
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And if the patient has a cold hand in warm water, as long as the pulse is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound more loosely, so that the vein opens well, and then do the same without making it too wide or narrow.</start_of_turn>
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if it cannot be passed without damage, keep the hand in warm water, and leave the blood to flow freely until enough has drained out.</start_of_turn
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	if it is in this state, do not force the hand into the warm water, because more harm will be done in doing so.</start_of_turn
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	the blood of this vein is more useful than that of all the others, for there is neither artery nor nerve.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The saliva from the right hand is worth for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the manner:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	The hand is strained, and held in hot water, until the vein is emptied; if it is seen

Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	When the patient has a cold fever, and his joints are swollen from the heat, and the veins are full of blood; and if the veins are in the ankle, or below the knee, from there comes drops of urine; the same as if there were a large wound there, or at the ankle, that the urine comes out in greater quantity.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you keep it warm from the cold that comes from outside, and the health of the passage is as if you were cutting; and be careful not to burn it.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be put back, if you reset the bone in the water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its saliva is that the patient should be immersed in hot water, and wipe over the vein until it turns pale, and press below the joint of the bone.</start_of_turn
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And if the vein is at the ankle, and below the bone there comes out a rain of blood.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	healthy blood, then there is either a large or small rain, or at the ankle, that the limb is pale.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you are healthy below the bone, if you watch over the nerves that are soaked, and the health passes through just as if you were catching it;
et soit li flaimes anesil.	or the fire is extinguished.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient drinks or bathes, and the wound is strained at the ankle for two thumbs, for otherwise it will not open; and if it opens, do so in all ways you can, and through and through; and it is better that you close it, for the wound is already sore, and it is better to leave it alone with the hands.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	and if the patient must be treated for the first time, if it starts again later at the same time, because the wound is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and do the same with the other limb equally
des sainies de ventouse	of air bubbles.</start_of_turn
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	and if the patient is suffering from pain or swelling, and if the limb is twisted twice at the ankle, because otherwise the vein will not open;

Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	But if you do not hold her tightly, if he can neither lift her nor bring her down, nor towards the little toe, nor protect her from the nails;

Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to wind, or by custom, if the physician notes that the patient has coughed for some hour at the beginning or at the end of a month, or at any time, and if he makes a grimace or sighs in every tension; for there are some who, when they must wind, have a heavy head; and some who feel swelling and redness in their face, and in their head and at the collar, and dark circles under their eyes; and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth and have spit out the tongue and vomited blood. And some who dream of these things and see nothing but blood and death and fear and many other things.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Blisters are made of horn, or hair, or wool;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and a wound is made in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by burning and drawing out blood, or by cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	Or by burning and drawing out blood, or by cutting. And this wound which is made by cutting is in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is with great heat, or by cutting.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the wound which is made by cutting and by drawing out blood is done in twelve palms of pain, from which one is all over the head of the sufferer.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is at the collarbone
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two on two ribs of the collarbone
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the wound of the face is loosened from the chin
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the wound of the two scapulae
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the catgut on the crupies;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the sponges on the armpits; and the sponges cover both arms.

Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The wind blowing in the neck is in lieu of blood from the head and from the brains, and for this reason it is worth to extend the pressure of the thumb, to open the channel of the beard, and in all things, and to cause swelling; and it is to be known that if it is held too tightly, it can cause strangulation or swelling of the stomach or the chest.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	When the moisture of the marrow helps with the pain of the head … that comes from the swelling, and it does not suffice to do anything before evacuating all the pus.

Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the cautery is that you must first make an empty wound, and then immediately apply it, and hold it firmly, and move it equally, and do not stop until you see the flesh red and swollen, and open the blood vessel

Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui. Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain occurs, if it is urgent to save the patient’s life on one side or the other, if nothing else can be done, if there is weakness of the limbs, or if the patient is a feeble or old person; or if the tension is not very strong or too cold; and mix cold baths, that is to say cold showers, and oil and laurel bath, and do not drink wine, do not eat fatty foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that there is no further risk of fracture or swelling of the limb. For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones that are broken into pieces and decrepit cannot well rejoin or unite according to their nature because of the drying up of the limbs; neither can those that are too brittle, like bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no remedy, hold above the broken bone the great tension which appears and unite the limb together, as long as it endures as before.</start_of_turn>
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not move from its place, for this reason we must nourish it with large foods, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And sometimes there is a sign that indicates its fracture, and its own instrument in restoration, as it is remembered; and it is known that the breaking of the bone is when it is twisted, and opens widely by pushing, and some by pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have twisting, or fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is impossible for me to move the limb, but you bring medicines that come after, then restrain it now cautiously.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the wounds which break that go into the marrow, and are two parts of the joint, it is now necessary to put them right equally, even as abscesses which come afterwards; and if abscesses come afterwards, if you leave no mark, as long as the abscess is appeased; then put them right alongside the bone as you wish gently and safely, and the wounds which restored themselves are more gentle than those which remained there or had parts. Then strain, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And at times there is its own remedy and its own instrument in its restoration, according to what is remembered to come in its place.</start_of_turn
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the breaking of the bone is by this that it is twisted, and opens well by force, and some by pressure of the hand.</start_of_turn
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no swelling or touch, and the patient does not feel much pain, there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but he may well have swelling, or tear, or a small fracture.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to him that it is not well: if the swelling is good and does not constrain him too much, do not press so much as they do who make it come by their work an abscess and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And the bones that are fractured that go inwards, and are two parts of the joint, it is necessary to put them back in place equally, even as if it were alive;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if there are abscesses that come, if you leave them whole, as long as the abscess is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it back in place at the shoulder as gently and cautiously as possible, and the bones that are restored are lighter than those that were fractured or broken
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then the constraint, if it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones, if they extend two parts, if it is the hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or two strings, or one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb that are broken are unbent, if you remain with all your senses the adnexes to its place as much as possible, and keep that in your work does not cause the patient pain or injury
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel well at the hand if you think that it is not well:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If the wound heals well, and is not too tightly bound, do not press so much as those who make it come by their work at an abscess with swelling and contraction in the limb.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is stiff, if the patient feels pain that does not move, neither day nor night, neither turning nor otherwise;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	Beware that the limb is well secured so that it does not cause him any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you can put it in order so that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And keep it properly positioned, so that no torsion arises when you restore it.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	The condition of the limb is as I have told you.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the splint that one puts upon the fracture be greater and broader than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the limb in breadth or length; then strain over the toes in the same way as before; and tie under a thread without fail, as before under the fracture; the more tightly it is bound, the less. And let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of linen; for if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their threads of linen cord, that is a great mistake, because the thread will not be equal if it is too subtle, and it will not hold properly.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For indeed there are small members, such as arms and thighs and the like:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	for indeed it is proper to cover them with soft and fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as knees and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	for indeed it is proper to cover them with a broad and firm bandage, for the large bandages embrace the whole great limb and constrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no bulge
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then keep the limb still for three rounds or four, as it is convenient for the limb, and constrain the hand one inch above the break, and then go below the break and constrain less, than the break itself will slip away a little
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the limb somewhat and somewhat, until you take a great part of the pain away, and then take hold of another limb and turn the dislocation back in its place
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then draw again at the lower part of the fracture, and strain moderately, not too strong nor too weak, as we said before.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put between the broken bones some bands of linen or bandages, so that they are all even, and then bind them up above with strong bands, and then put on your splints well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, put on above something soothing the abscess, which softens the swelling, and leave it to soak for a while;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your splints, and let them be half as wide as a broad thumb, or of a staff from which nails are made, or of hemp seeds, and let them be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the support that is put on the fracture be greater and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And be of equal length as it is necessary for the limb in its entirety or in its breadth;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then it is strained upon the supports just as you did at the first hour, and then you should tie it down with a thread immediately, as you did at the first hour on the fracture
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The tighter it is bound, the less.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it must be that the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is thick, like those fools who make their nets of linen cord, that is a great mistake, because the bandage will not be even if it is too fine, and it will not hold properly except with a space between the supports less than two fingers wide.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is great, it is not proper to put these stakes in place except after five days or seven, or more according to the severity of the afterburn; and when this is done, the method of ancient plasters is useful for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: take some flour that is kept beside the mill, mix it with an abundance of eggs, and make this confection, not too thick nor too thin, and use it. This is the common method of plastering that restores fracture in many positions, and is equally useful for women and for small children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of dressing that restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains, linseed, alum, saffron, and Arabic gum, and mix them with vinegar; mix mirra and aloes, with vinegar; mix alechil with vinegar; and grind them up, and mix them with eggs; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this dressing, for it is made of good materials and will restore the fractured bones quickly, and is worth more than many homes.

Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to soothe joints and bones that are swollen from their swelling, and to relieve pain, is to use oil of bones and bruise them, and to use ointment made from bones and meal, and to apply pressure to the wound, and to break it.

Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to soothe bones that have been broken:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry fig leaves and terrestrial marshmallow leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of chamomile, and flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and fennel, and violets and chamomile flowers, all in equal parts; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of chamomile, marigolds, violet flowers, barley flour, rue, one part of fennel seed;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind them, mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, mix with wet coriander juice, or water, and use it as needed.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen deems that one must put something warm upon the broken limb to restore it, such as wax and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take root of chamomile, flaxseed, marshmallow, balm, melilot, violet and chamomile flowers, all of which are equal parts
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Grind them, mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little later, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone of the limb moved; if not, loosen by hand for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, sense rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen it, and stabilize the displacement immediately; and apply a light bandage, and a wet sponge of sea salt, and immerse in water, and lift up the limb, until the swelling ceases, and the pain is calmed; then leave the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry lint, moistened in water or oil of rose, and bind with a nut, until you are certain that the abscess has gone; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and make the pain cease, then recommence the gentle manipulation, and another displacement, and do not strain it so much as before; and be discreet until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see swelling, redness, pain and swelling around the bone, and that it is renewed, as you did the first time, you must provide support and lian, if necessary.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Other methods of treatment that are worth more than lesions and pain:

Other methods of treatment that are worth more than lesions and pain: take mugwort and chopped onions, or henbane seeds, and vinegar, and mix them evenly, and grind them, and make a poultice of it and apply it liberally.
