et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And do it discreetly until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of fractures are seen, and various figures, and the causes are manifold; for there are fractures caused by the percussion of a spear, and the collar bone fractured throughout to the syphus which is the socket of the bone, as in the case of a fracture by splinters; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a "haichure".
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if there is no improvement in the limb after the things we have said, if you do not see it recover after three days or four, or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	never leave it twenty days, as we have seen, until the swelling has gone down, and approach the setting of the limb slowly.</start_of_turn>
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Therefore greater restraint must be used than before, and it engulfs the flesh, as I have already said.
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb dry out more than usual, the flesh swells up, it will not be able to come out.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	it will rise with a hot water bath every time you stretch it, and even if you do it every third hour, you will cut through the ligament
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	because in this work, the limb must be pulled out from the member, and it must be strongly supported to prevent what the fools do, who return the limb crookedly
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	it is bad, and if it is done carelessly, I see nothing else but to leave it loose and give up directly.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or fracture or displacement of the bone, or swelling on the bone, or other similar things.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many are the ways of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	for there are fractures caused by percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone all the way to the socket which is the marrow of the bone, as in the case of a splinter or fracture.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a «splinter».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or when the spear pierces the bone from below in a forward direction, and is called this kind of fracture «absolute».
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And there are wounds of these two kinds, great or small.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have soft bones or heads of children; and it happens in all these ways that small pieces are loosened from them like stars; and I will speak of it in detail later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And thus, we know of all these breaks by the tearing above them, the questioning of tensions, and the corrupt matter which is above.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is closed in the bone as subtly as a louse, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called a «capillary» fracture
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made by fire, or by injury of stone, or by thorn, or by any other similar thing, and causes the piece of bone under to enter, and the head of the limb is bent as when they are heated over a cauldron.
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the teeth of the bone is something.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And that which comes after has moist bones or soft flesh, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	it comes to all these fractures that small pieces are detached from each other as stars
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an imminent accident, and you hope for health, if so, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the limb comes first to you, and it is in the armpit, if so, it is right to remove the bone from its fourteenth part from the muscle that you must touch.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this state, if you are hasty to remove the bone from its seventh part from the bone that you must touch, then the tissue of the bone will be corrupted, and there will come the accident that we have mentioned.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a break of the bone comes up to the scalp that covers the brain, if you do that, you must cut off the split part: and that is that you take the head of the patient and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and on the figure of the wound more deeply than you can; and if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or incisions, do what is useful, and that you fill the wound with moist cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the incisions have subsided, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then when the fracture has been set, it is done in two ways: one way if the nail of the fracture is narrow in front, and that is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture which is greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And so, if you have various sized nails, some thin and some thick, and they are pointed or iron-tipped, and in lighter work, that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the cloth that covers the brain, then you must make the fractured part whole again
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And it is that you take hold of the patient’s hand and uncover the bone in every way that you can, and on the figure of the wound more thoroughly than you can; and if blood comes from uncovering the bone, or from an abscess, if it helps, and that you fill the cavity with cloths soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	And rest the wound until the abscesses have subsided, and be sure of the evacuation of blood;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	Then begin to support the bone, and this is done in two ways:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	The first way is if the tail of the fracture is narrow in front, and this is the form
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through a brittle bone is that you put one washer on the bone, and turn your thumbs until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the washer back in another place a little later, and do everything around, and close the incisors of the space between the holes, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you have reached the bone in your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like pliers, pincers; and keep that you do not touch the brain or the jaw.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	The second way is if there are many pieces of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and iron-bound
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in lighter work, do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is tough and hard, if you must pierce through, then you must know that you must pierce through only as much as the bone will bear, and must leave on the edge a margin or a circle, that does not leave the point pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	You must also have several of these, so that when the marrow comes out from the thickness of the bone, if you have sponges over all the test;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	These are the three forms of sponges:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The one that qualifies to pierce through the brittle bone is that you put one sponge on the bone, and twist your two hands until you feel that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then he puts his thumb back in another place a little after, and then he makes all the surrounding area taut, and then he cuts through the space of the bone which is between the holes, and he does this more subtly than you would think, and lightly, as we have said, until you have brought the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have like tenailles, clamps.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And keep your fingers away from the brain and the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have grasped the bone, and treated, if you can, reset the fragment which has come loose from the bone to any other instrument resembling a chisel, but it must be more firm and subtle than the other chisel
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if it does not stay in any of the small bones, do not attempt to extract any fragments, if the bone is lightly held by any instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with stitches and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	Or another way of working if it is known that Galen speaks of this, which is more useful.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the limb is very strong, and that is his word
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is much scraping beforehand, and afterwards more subtly, and does not cease doing so until it is well done
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not tear from one side, but from the two costs, so that if you tear from the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then hold a small mallet above, so that you can easily break the bone without damaging the skin that is below;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is close to the bone, if you break it easily, because we must break it gently and without pain
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the tip of the jaw is discovered, take a drape of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in olive oil, and put it on the wound; then take another drape doubled in two or three, and wet it in wine and olive oil, and put it on the first drape; and do this more gently than you can, that you do not damage the jaw, then administer by mouth another line of medicine, and do not restrain it more than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for one or two days, until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines such as root of iris, and oatmeal, and incense powder, and an apothecary, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer adequate medicines with the taste of medicine. Keep the wound clean, do not leave it bloody, do not leave it to gather pus, for when pus gathers on the wound it swells and causes great harm; for when anything biting is put on the jaw, if it is not done by mouth.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there be any doubt or suspicion.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	As for other surgeons and breakers of bones, it is appropriate that you bring the cause according to its location;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	It is a thing that has no parallel among those who have studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	If the disease is discovered, then you must take a drape of lint, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another drape of lint doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first drape
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this more gently than you would, so as not to damage the disease, then administer further support below the limb, and do not hold it too tightly except as much as is necessary to hold the wound in place only
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And leave it in place for a while or two, until the swelling of the wound has subsided, then remove it, and administer medicines such as licorice root, alum, powdered incense, and an astringent, and similar things
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And from these things make powder, put it on the wound, and administer besides medicines of a lawful kind in accordance with the biting.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And keep that the wound is closed properly, that you do not leave it open, neither do you leave it unclosed, for when it is closed over the brain, if it is crooked and twisted, it brings great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	For when you put on the teeth of biting things, if they do not desist from below.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if it is prudent that you swallow your small toe or nail, and put equal healing into your index finger and the pouch by driving it out, until it returns to its natural position; and do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if black bile does not go away except by the medicine that we have put on, that a part of virtue has remained, so it is appropriate that you take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue I drape, and put it on the teeth of biting.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment for these things must be such that when they are healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	So that at no time are the two parts of the bone broken, or one by one, because these are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And this is because cartilage does not break, unless forced by swelling or bending, and then it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, if you must bite your thumb or pierce the bone, and put the break back into its place at the index finger and the palm by force, until the bone returns to its natural position.</start_of_turn
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain from your work.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should mingle the tents in the burrow, and die each for himself.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is two parts, if you make another one, hasten to restore the first one if you wish.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling of the wound has subsided, then bind the head of the limb so that it does not attempt to pull the fragments of the fracture apart, if the fracture is in one part.</start_of_turn>
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or if you break another part, if the fracture is through and through.</start_of_turn
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let the attempts be so strong that they fill the hole of the wound.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if it happens that pus comes with snow while you are working, if you put some butter or cotton soaked in rose oil, or some vinegar.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not know that it is good, but it seems to me that they must be soft in composition like eggshell and fine powder.</start_of_turn
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the hair, until the bones are firm and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never do we or do not put goose feathers in place of hair, and if there is even a slight breeze that blows, and if the eye is held steady, blow on the patient among them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make them cough as you see.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and there is no break of the bone, except for the teeth which are loosened, if you know it lightly.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the pus does not come, if you put in plaster of Paris, oatmeal powder, and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then put on soft bandages, and do not bind too tightly;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the fracture is slight and is broken into small pieces, if the extractor has suitable instruments, then cover the wound, and close the wound with stitches, and suture with dressings and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he has no wound or swelling, if he cures from tension, and he puts on linen patches, as long as he is well.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in.ij., if you must, that you administer extension of.ij. parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth comes about, or a fracture, if strained by a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place a broken mandible cerate on and place over it a pair of doubled drapes; and over the drapes place a large well-made sponge, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and bind it to the tooth that you wish, and command the patient to rest, and feed on soft food.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is appropriate, if the fracture is on the lower part, that you bite your thumb against the patient’s mouth.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the left mandible, if you hold your right thumb of the right hand, and hold the fracture lightly, and do it with the other hand forward, and keep it even.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if postoperative swelling comes, if we have said it often before.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, if there is strain from a golden or silver or silken thread, then put on the fractured mandible a cerate and put on a double drape.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And put on the drape a great star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it on the bone as you please, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft foods.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	If you see that the limb is crooked, if you pull it out at the shoulder, and then reset it to its original position;
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	put a poultice on it, with coarse powder of rye or oatmeal, after you have oiled the bone well with butter.</start_of_turn>
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	put on a layer of linen bandage, and if the poultice is too tight, and the patient's condition does not improve, leave it as it is until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	many times it heals in three weeks.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have solidified all these fragments, and there is no more movement, if the wound is wide, put on some covering instruments to prevent pain, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	and if there is a break and wound together, support the fractured piece so that it becomes solid.</start_of_turn
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the subtlety of the bone has established firm coventions on this one.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceful rupture has occurred several times previously in this area, near the shoulder, and if it is broken in two places, there are pieces, and it is more light to restore; or if there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the break is when there is a wound, you must have two assistants, so that one holds the limb that feels the forceful rupture; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then put the break back in its place so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor swelling.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend further, put under the patient’s shoulder a round ball of wax, or linen, as thick as you need; and extend and hold the forceful rupture, and strain the ball with your hand, so that you can put the break back in its place as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and breaks if it is in three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or it is broken and loosened in two pieces, and there are fragments, and it is easier to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is a break with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is when the break is in the direction of the wound, that you have two assistants, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the force of the break;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the limb towards the part
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then put the break even at your shoulders, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you must extend further, put a round ball of wax or lint on the patient's shoulder; make it large as needed.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and hold the forceps, and strain the ball at your hand, so that you break it evenly, as it should be.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If the wound runs deep, if there is much blood, apply oil of roses, aloe, and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	Then direct the break to your side, and if you find debris, if it comes to that, you must make an incision above.</start_of_turn
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and withdraw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be rejoined by any means, if the socket has reached one of your incisors.</start_of_turn
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but hold the forceps steady, for this is the instrument to prevent the blood from clotting.</start_of_turn
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	And it seems like a scoop, but is not so wide, and be as large as it ought to be, according to the size of the bone and the capacity of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And has two holes, as you see, and one is large, and the other is small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the position of the cautery, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the position of the cautery, if you find the wound of cloth and stitches, according to their quantity
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the scapula is broken or widened, do not pull it out by force except by touch; if the limb appears according to the fracture pattern, and is reset according to its natural form, in all ways as you wish; then put on the limb powder with abundance of eggshell, and bandage lightly, and put on a double drape; then put on a broad and subtle staple, a little wider than the scapula, and when the staple is fixed firmly in no part of the scapula, if you use the staple of hemp, so that the staple rests evenly; and then strain it with a great firm bend, so that the staple does not move from its place, and watch the skin of each joint; and every time it swells, if you strain, and put the staple back in its place if it has come loose from its place, and lie the patient down on his side; and the scapula is restored in twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if the bone is fractured, and so be careful, for this is not a bone that easily breaks.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The stiffness of the bone, when it is painful and tight, is that you put on the bone the plaster of the fine powder of mill and egg-white, and put on soft stamps below, and put a sponge of soap on the heel, if you have need of it.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very great bend of a palm of a broad kind, then put on two layers over the toes, and place it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a slender rod of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that palm, so that the head of the palm rests during;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And put the rod on the heel, and turn the palm on the collarbone, and loosen the tight flesh, and loosen the painful flesh.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And hold the shoulder firmly in place, and when you see that the limb holds the heel firmly, and you clearly see that the rod does not move from the heel bone, if you reward every joint, and when you see that the limb is straightened, if the restraint is maintained
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And make the patient lie on his back, and put under his buttock a little cushion, to lift the shoulder up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If you align the break of the scapula with the alignment of the shoulder, or if you bind the arm to the collarbone, and do not loosen it until it is better, for up to twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then reapply the bandage if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it in place until it is restored
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in about eight days, and less to no homes.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone thrust forward, and not a little like before, if it stays there, and the bone, do as we said at the fracture of the forceps to appease the afterburn.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	There is only that the shoulder is broken or displaced from its place, and that you must not touch it except by treatment
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If the limb appears according to the figure of the fracture, and is reset according to its natural form, in all the ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then take out the limb powder of wheat with abundance of eggs, and bind loosely, and put on a double bandage
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then put on a broad and subtle splint, a space wider than the shoulder, and keep the splint firm in no part of the shoulder, if you use this support of towings of flax, so that the splint remains even
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then keep it tightly bound around a great bend firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the limb frequently

et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in twenty days or in twenty-five.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When this time has passed, if the dislocation has not already healed, and the limb is still stiff, for it is not a bone that has moved too lightly.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, if it declines downward, and causes the patient great pain, and there is no relief, vomiting blood, and loosening teeth in the fractured bone, and all this together.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a piece of the bone thrust forward, and not a little like before, if it stays there, and the bone, do as we said at the fracture of the forceps to appease the afterburn. And the restoration is that the patient lies again on his back, and puts in between the scapulae, then presses the scapulae, and reassembles the two ribs at the hands, and discreetly put all in equal manner that the figure of the bone is as it should; then put on bandages and bandage below the staple of salt, or other soft matter, and cover with a bandage, and bind above the fractured bone, so that it does not move; and turn the patient around the back, and restrain him gently, and reward somewhat every hour that the limb is loose, and if it relaxes, restrain it; and if you see that it is loosening, due to corrosion or by inflammation that comes to the limb, or pain or swelling, do not hesitate, and loosen it, and scrape away the dressing, and address what has come from the manner of treatment; then remend the dressing, and restrain it until it is healed.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The limb is never broken in the middle, but this often happens
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it breaks often at the end
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The ribs that break from the breast only come from the back, at the shoulder and do not bend except because they are slimy; and the pain is well known at the inquiry of two.

puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put on dressings and support the delicate part of the salt, or another soft material, and cover it with a bandage, and bind it over the broken bone, so that it does not move

puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then rest the wound, and hold it firm until it is healed.</start_of_turn>

Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	The wounds that break the ribs do not come from their great extent after the back, and at the head downwards, but only because they are slippery.</start_of_turn
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And he feels quite well at the inquiry as two.</start_of_turn>
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who say it must administer food that swells the belly, to push out the pain at its departure.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after these chills have passed, life does not come again if it has not already begun.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the ribs break downwards, the patient experiences great pain, and points, as with tears, because the bone points at the gut.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And there is vomiting and spitting out great amounts of blood, which is a grievous matter, and the old ones put in great effort.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that no one has ever put a bandage on the body to stop the fever, for it is like reason; however, there is doubt that the bandage will not draw out the superfluous humours from the body by the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that on must not cover the wound with coarse linen soaked in oil, but put on tents between the ribs to make equal the hour around, then either cure with the treatment for pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points towards the armpit, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is necessary to open the skin of the fractured bone, and if it is necessary to place a bandage, then one must cut through the bone, treat it gently, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with dressings until it is healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	They say that no one has ever seen a wound heal without causing harm, because it is similar to reason

Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The wounds are mortal in many cases, and if you move them and feel well when you extract them and prick them, the union of the bone is saved, and the patient will be healed, if we put on treatment

et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And also at the spine of the back
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is reminded on the back and it is seen to be limp, it cannot be cured.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	The wounds are mortal: if you do not work diligently in their cure
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if anything similar comes to the spine of the back, and you see that it is neither healthy nor sick, if you take care that the pieces are softened, and if the accident is that which is in the hands, and on the back there is wind and vomiting spontaneously;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it is applied to the belly, if the patient suddenly evacuates against his will.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is less serious. If there is swelling, put on rose oil or yolk of egg on the spine; when it is calmed down, put on a comfortable and drying dressing, and bind it with a bandage, and tell the patient to rest; do not sleep on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	It is deadly to him.
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if he does not toil in his cure.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the bone of the thigh

et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the bone, then join the two layers of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, and then cure with ointment containing herbs, as long as it is necessary;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone is broken, which is called the «fracture of the marrow», if you hold your fist with your left hand and put it equal to the other hand at your side, and put the bandage and the support on, if necessary.

And if the fracture is long or declines downwards, make the patient lie on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	There is only one case in which the thigh bone is broken, and if it happens, there must be some sign of injury at the head of the bone.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And keep it long, and decline at the root, and comes to the patient pain in the limb, point and swelling, which breaks it.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And if you extend your hand over it, as long as you are over the wound;
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	And the hair which is the wound and the figure of the limb;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the wound is at the head only, if you make it even, as long as it is in a natural position.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscess bursts, do not touch it, until the abscess has subsided; then put on what we have mentioned before; and then return to rest, and hold it still if it is appropriate, without causing any further harm; this is the proper method.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have put it even, put over the limb a cushion of wool or fur, and hold the wound, so that it does not move
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And keep the limb still against the ribs, as long as the wound is even
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if the boil breaks open, do not touch it until the boil has calmed down, and put on what we said before.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	Then return to the restoration and tighten it if it is necessary, without causing any further harm.
et c’est li maniere.	That is all.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one should order the attendants to hold the limb firmly at its collar and to grasp the limb above the elbow with the fist of the hand that is not supporting it, and to hold down the forearm with the other hand, and to extend the forearm to its greatest extent.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulder joint is supported by the tissue between the shoulder blade and the head of the humerus, and if it is fractured, it must be restored in one of two ways:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one of which is to take one fist full of myrrh, according to this fashion
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	and bind the two fingers together, and hold the limb high, and support the patient on his seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then the shoulder joint hangs limply down to the elbow, as far as the elbow joint, and has in it a swelling of the elbow; then it rests upon no heavy object or the attendant extends the forearm.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then he puts his hands together, and makes the swelling even; so that the swelling returns as it should.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the wound does not come out, do not strain for more than thirteen days; put on a soft bandage and oil of rose, until the wound is calmed; then strain, and put the support on the bone, then assemble the limb on the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put on the bandage, strain on the aid, and on the limb, so that the limb is in its place, without anything hindering it, or without displacing the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not displaced, if you use pins, put on the bone a pin wider and stronger than the others, and leave between the pins a space equal to twice the thickness of the bone; then strain on the pins, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter, more strongly and less loosely.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the swelling is close to the head of the shoulder, if you must put a little pressure from the elbow towards the shoulder, and another from the shoulder towards the elbow, from the swelling.</start_of_turn
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And thus if the swelling is towards the shoulder, if you must put a little pressure lightly, gently, so that the swelling is even on the limb and on the shoulder.</start_of_turn
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then put them even, if it is possible, and hold them, because if they do not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if they do come out, if it does not come out by itself, hold them for seven days, and put on soft linen and rose oil, until the abscess is calmed;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then hold them, and put the dressing on the break, and reassemble the limb on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the side
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	Then put the bandage, and hold the shoulder on the dislocation, and on the limb, so that the limb is stable, without anything hindering it, or without moving the bone.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use sticks; place a thicker and stronger stick above the break and leave between the sticks one space equal to the thickness of three sticks; and let one stick be as thick as to pass through the break three times from the stick side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then strain upon the sticks, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter concerning the break above the break, stronger and less flexible.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the settling of the sticks and the tightening, as we have said, while restoring the limb after the break, and if you doubt the fracture, let it bind until the seventh day, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look for three days in a row that the limb is neither swollen nor painful, or that the discolorations do not come to the limb because it is too stiff.</start_of_turn
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is painful and bloody, if it remains for more than a day or two months.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents occur, if only after three days or more, let the patient lie down on his back, and rest his hands on his stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	Put the shoulder in its natural position immediately, while it is still firm and straight, and watch for an hour or so to see if the limb remains properly aligned, or if the ligaments are softened
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if necessary, with the help of medicine, and do the thing which is before us, partly as if it were at the first moment
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And when it begins to recover, even if it is slightly
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	It is customary that the shoulder and limb should be taken hold of for forty days in all cases
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And therefore you must immediately loosen [the dislocation] and administer baths and ointments to the affected limb.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are fractured, restoration is easy, and healing; but when the large bone is fractured, if the healing is bad, it is more painful than when it is fractured whole.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is fractured, if it is recommended to extend the limb slightly, and put it equal.</start_of_turn>
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the «humerus» and the «ulna», of which one is small and is connected to the pouch.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	The other is large, and is connected to the shoulder blade below the little toe;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance the large bone simply breaks, or the small one, or both together
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bone is broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the large bone is broken, if it is fractured alone, the healing is worse than when it is fractured together with the small bone.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If in the fracture it is broken into pieces, if you put something into its place, and if there is none that pricks it now, and you do not manage to restore it to its place, if you leave it and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the great bone, if the coving must be more forceful.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and the handle is placed over the cusp, and grasp the pouch of the hand above the others, and the little finger must go lower than the others, and let the patient cross over on himself, and the cusp will be in front of him above, so that the patient does not feel any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the limb from the armpit to the outside of the hand, or to the elbow, and another assistant at the other side below
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration blood spurts out, if it is thick I cover it with a coating of rose oil and white wax, neither too thick nor too thin; and I cover it from above secretly, until the spurting blood has ceased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then I apply the cerote, and I place a stuffing of fine powder with eggshells, because I put in the pins, and let the pin of the bone be more firm and wider than the others; and I make the wound have six pins or more in various positions: either that the fracture is in one of the bones, or in two; and I stretch it more on the fracture than elsewhere, and I keep it together less often, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the draping that is on the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, which is used to tie it, be neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	and if with the forceps for wounds, as I have already spoken to the singular chapter.
si pren la cure.	take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	and if during the commencement of restoration blood comes out from the incisions, if the drape is glued with cerate made of rose oil and white wax, that it be neither too thick nor too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And thus I recommend that you suspend the incisions for a while, until the pain from the aftershocks has subsided.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then I order the bones to be closed, and I put the dressing of powdered meal with much egg, because I put the needles in place, and let the needle of the trocar be more firm and a little wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and the stitches that must be taken must be six needles or more in various positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	or that the trocar is in one of the bones or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	And is more strained above the armpit than elsewhere, and all the days less in aligning, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	And let the hair be soft that is above the armpit, moist and not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And let the thread that is strained be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said before
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling does not depart from the limb, because it is too great, then shalt thou soften it, namely by fomentation, and let it remain for some days, until the swelling depart, and then restrain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if other ailments come to the limb, if there is itching that comes to the limb, you must raise the limb with warm water, until the itching is appeased
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And let the limb be neither too tight nor too loose
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when the swelling has gone down, then let the patient hold his hands to his collar, and keep his collar even, and protect him from movement and contamination, and sleep on his back; and give him nourishment every thirty days or every fifty, or sometimes every twenty days, according to the composition and temperament of the virtues
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The bones at the back of the hand and two together cause many fractures, and only rain comes more often.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or else if it is twisted, then put the hands to the collar and let the collar be even, and be careful of movement and vomiting, and sleep on the back
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And the wounds that this fracture has caused are restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and sometimes in XX days, according to the composition and complexion of the virtues.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is at the shoulder blade under the belly of the limb, if you make a ball of cloth, and command the patient to hold his broken limb against his side; then strain from a long cloth, and be the splint as great as the limb, and strain it, as it is commanded.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is downwards, if you command me to place a splint above and another below, so that the hand is overspread and straight, then I will bind it tightly around the hand, and hold it between the two.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the bone of the arm is broken or dislocated, if it is necessary, let the patient sit steadily, and look straight ahead equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then put the hand on the extended cloth, and extend the minister the fractured bones, and put them equal to the eyes, until they are well joined
