et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And be covered with a linen bandage.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the edge near the belly of the bone, if you make a loop of gauze, and command the patient to pull it at his fractured bone
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Then the stretching of a long hair, and if the staple of marrow is as great as the leaf of the hand, and the stretching, if it can.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the hip are often fractured, and one can see it when it turns frontward and backward; and the restoration is when it is bound together again.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if it breaks out to neither of us two, if it is the marrow pouch, if you put it even, if it can.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	And the stretching with the leaf, and if you see that you put a right little staple to raise the break, and it does not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	And if the break is like the others two, as in the index or the other, if you put it even, and tie it with the two healthy things that are after;
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	Or you hold them together with holding, that the muscle is worth it, or you put on a staple, as if it were a pouch
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And take care in restoring and arranging the cautery after it is finished, and cure whatever comes of it as I have said.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if a fracture is close to the root of the thigh, if one of the ligaments above the ankle is broken, and the other ligament below the fracture.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The shoulder blade is often fractured, and one can see it when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And the restoration must be firm, so that it does not break again in the future.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	The patient lies on his face, then stretches out his limbs equally wide
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	It is when the fracture is in the bone itself
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a strong bandage doubled over twice or three times, and to remove the excess, then bend the limb until the talons reach the root of the nail, and pass a thread long between the thigh and the limb below the knee, from below the knee up to the top; then bend the limb and the thigh together, and put on the outer dressing and a stay.  Then put two threads of the same kind between the thigh and the limb as you passed before, and three stays that are below, and put back the thread at the top until you see below the piece; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any further damage.</start_of_turn>
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is close to the elbow, then either the forearm is fractured or the arm is extended backwards
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then put the bones in their natural position, and then put on the bandage and bind it securely so that it does not move
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a wound above, if you leave it calm and then return to your work and your cure.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is done in a partial manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is fitting that you wrap around the bruise with a bandage doubled in two or three, and hold the excess, then stretch the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail, and put a long thread between the hip and the limb, without loosening the knee, and keep the head of the thread below;
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then tighten the bandage on the limb and on the hip, and put on the external bandage, and put a pin on the bone of the limb
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then employ between the limb and the hip a cloth of soft cloth to make it even, and start to tie three or four knots above the wound
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And the more you go beyond the limit, and the less you restrain;
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then as two hairs of a thread that you have placed between the leg and the hip, and there are three stars that are below, then raise the hand to the head of the thread, as long as you see beneath the bone.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and the restraint, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not cause any incision or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if there is any loosening, if it comes loose, address that which comes, as we have said many times before.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that prick, if you cover them, it is useless;
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	If it cannot stay in place, if it is necessary, cut the limb and draw out the bone.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, so that it may be healed
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never is the limb broken in this way when we put in place the bones, as in the shoulder and the arm
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	although in the restoration made here I do not harm the patient.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	If they break, if not only a tear, or an opening, and there is pain, swelling, and this feels very well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane.
de la brisure de la jambe	And thus, if you put everything that is round back to its place, as long as it is put together firmly, then put the dressing on and place a round cushion there if you have need of it, and hold it firmly, then restore all the other things that we have mentioned before, such as an abscess incision and other similar things; if you put each accident in its place that it deserves, as long as it is sane.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hairs that on the leg have two bones, of which one is called the "muscle" and the other is called the "fleshy part"; and they often break as it happens with the arm, and for this reason the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the work is all done in this way. And if both bones are fractured together, the leg is twisted in every part
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	and the restoration is made when the round parts are put back in their place, as long as the bones are properly aligned
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	then place the bandage and put a round pin in, if you need it, and hold it as it should be held, then reward all the instructions we have said before, as in cautery and the like
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If one meets with an accident of this kind that is still sane.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the great bone is fractured, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it is twisted from its place.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	If one meets with an accident of this kind that is still sane, such as when there are two bones in the limb, of which one is called the “muscle” and the other is called the “foscile”.
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and there is a fracture in its entirety as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is as if it were the same limb, and the work is all the same. Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once you have completed your work, if you take two strips of coarse cloth that reach from under the armpit to under the knee of the limb, and bind the limb from one end to the other; then cover with two layers of bandage from under and over, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not be able to move forward or backward; and that is good; and no one should administer anything that will lengthen the limb, and if there is swelling, and it is a fracture, and there are many pieces, that the extension should be less violent and lighter; and adjust accordingly.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is fractured, one feels great pain, and it is well seen
et torne desoz.	and is twisted about

et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the limb should be positioned according to your skill.

Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two breaks, if you restore them as we have said must be done with the hand; then put at the break a support according to the length of the break, and make it somewhat wider; and put on the thumb that which I have mentioned, and strain immediately; and if there are three or more breaks, break them, and put on over each break a support according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the thumb from the bone. Make sure that the thumb remains above the break of the bone as much as possible, if it remains well-held.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if there is a fracture of bones that are seen to be broken against each other, if you see these bones pressing on each other as if wanting to leave, put the limb on the earth like if it were going away, just as if it were an arrow that had gone astray; then put your limb back in its place, where the bones were raised, and press until they return to their sockets.</start_of_turn

si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if you give astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and saffron, acacia, and similar things, that you take none of these things, or all together, and mix them with a strong wine or with a lot of egg or with vinegar.</start_of_turn
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	And place it upon the knot in the armpit, and hold it firmly, and do not release it from your hands until it has healed.
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	Then dislocate it again, and repeat this process until the swelling subsides
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	Or you strain on a piece of soft tissue that is well done;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	For the property of soft tissue is that when it becomes stiff, it eliminates all the swellings under the limbs
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	When the swelling has turned into hardness like stone, and the swelling appears, it is necessary to pierce through, if the swelling above has subsided, and to make the excess visible.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Or do not touch it with any instrument, until it has become stiff, and cure it when it has healed.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the disease.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture has been restored, and remains firm after the limb has been weakened and straightened, if there is any cause for concern:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	or that it was too tightly bound and was not loosened as it should have been.
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or that there were too many bands and could not move freely on the limb
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or from excessive bruising.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or from too great movements that did not suit it in its place.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or from the presence of blood in the bone, if the limb is weak
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	The treatment is to make the patient rest and keep the limb firm until the pain subsides
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	And he administered a bath, and he did rejoice and delight.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then he put poultices on the limb, so that the poultices attract at the great nourishment, and swell often with hot water, until the nourishment comes to the limb.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returned to its natural shape
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Or do not cause movement to the limb immediately after its fracture
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after the restoration, and the bones are fractured open, and the limb is deformed, although it does not lose its natural work:
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have had this experience in our land
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	these works are blamed, and there comes great harm, and by chance the patient dies
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	Throughout, if swelling and torture are fresh, if it is known that they have arisen from hot water, or soft herbs are cooked, like fennel leaves, and radish, and honey, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and you make a soft poultice, like that of aquaint done well, and you take the nourishment of fennel, and confit with butter of marrow or oil of sesame, and make a poultice on it.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	or you take fat figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that soothe the swelling.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And thus begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the swelling is tough and hardened, like stone, and the bone is needed, if it is known to cover up to the bone, do the incision subtly;
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And put cushions and study in the treatment.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if it swells up, and by chance when it is reset, it causes pain to the limb; therefore it must not be moved while it is swollen: many times it brings about swelling and other pains; however, when this has happened, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, until the swelling has subsided; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and move it gently, and cure each limb as it comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have commanded the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder joint from the head to the wrist.</start_of_turn>
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if we delay, if the limb swells up, and by chance when we reset it, we cause pain in the limb.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Therefore it is not possible to move it while it is swollen
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	causing much pain and other aches
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	although when this happens, if you make the patient comfortable, then leave him, as long as the pain subsides;
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the limb gently and lightly, and cure each limb as it comes into its place
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns by itself in various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If it is entire and complete, you must certainly hold the limb firmly and without fear; and in such a way that the servant grasps the chief of the patient, and holds the thumb of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand must be placed flat, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them in all parts
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	For indeed, when the mandible is loosened and dislocation is imminent in both, there are two methods:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	Or they are a sign of bone looseness of their limbs, and soften them a little.
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Or they are completely loosened, and hang towards the lips, and cause him to salivate from the mouth that he cannot hold it, cannot close his mouth, and engulfs his tongue with speech.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it returns grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arise with hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not attempt to force it back, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entire and accompanied, if you must rejoin it immediately, do not delay me;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the minister grasps the head of the patient and keeps his eye on his pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands be bent down, to make them equal
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them from every side.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles do not manage to be reset at a single hour, and are not made firm at their roots, if in comes fever and swelling accustomed, and by chance vomiting of pure bile.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is gripped, even if both jaws are together, if they arise with acute heat and oil, until they remain lightly;
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not tear me away, as we have said
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are gently returned, and the patient’s mouth is properly closed with soft lips, put on moist cloths soaked in rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with linen threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on his back, and his arms rest between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, do not attempt to touch anything, but take light nourishment, until the pain is relieved, and the jaws are properly aligned
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	Then he must swallow what he wants lightly, and do not work to open his mouth wide while eating and drinking, until his jaw is well oiled and healthy.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot pull out a wound that is deeply seated, and is always damaged when it is driven out, and it is always felt.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	When you see this, know that it is a loss;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And often it causes death to him who has it, in seven days.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	De la dislocation de l’espaule.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Hairs that are too long at the shoulder are not loosened by anything except in three ways: Firstly, that they are loosened at the armpit downwards; and secondly, at the part of the wrist; and by chance at the part above, and this is enough; do not loosen them from behind the shoulder, or from the front, or more than once; and if several times they are loosened downwards towards the armpit, even among those who have little hair, for at these jumps they become immediately ill; and among those who have enough hair, the jumps become painful, and return to pain.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is when the patient lies still with his back on the ground, and extends his arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the limb that is towards your palm, and it will return
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then put on the bandage and the splint, and bind it tightly
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the one who is on the outside cannot unbuckle it.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	If not, and if it dislocates once more, if you leave it in its place as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then place the support and the bandage, and bind it, and restrain it, and command the patient to rest until he is well;
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And in this way the head of the shoulder is brought back to its place when it has been dislocated from its bone
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is necessary that you suspend it until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	When the shoulder blade is not dislocated except for three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	One is that it dislocates at the armpit downwards;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	And the second is at the painful side.
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	And often it is loosened at the upper part, and this is what usually comes about.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	And do not loosen behind for the scapula, and do not loosen from the bones;
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	And often it is loosened from the scapula downwards, even with those who have much hair, because of these jumps there is great suffering
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	with those who have enough hair, the jump is painful, and returns painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the physician grasps the painful limb upwards, then puts the thumbs downwards on the buttocks, and grasps the joint firmly upwards to the bone; and the physician grasps the limb and extends it upwards, since it is put downwards.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You must therefore believe it until you are certain;
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that dislocation is when it is tilted towards the buttocks, and distinguishes between the painful scapula and the sound one, and you will find between their diversity the manifestation
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow space, and loosen the shoulder blade from the bone of the shoulder, as if it were a bone.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you cannot make the patient move their arm to its place, or move it in any way
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	Also, if it is displaced upwards, if not hidden inside, because you will find it immediately by touch
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	This method of dislocation is not sufficient to restore it, when it is new, or when the patient is suffering
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	The method is that the physician holds the patient’s hand down, then places his thumbs under the shoulder blade, and holds the joint firmly upwards at the root;
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the minister holds the hand, and extends it upwards, because he puts on gloves.
si venra hastanment.	if there comes an illness.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	and if it does not come as we have said above, if you know that the patient is immersed in warm water;
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the minister gives soft and soothing nourishment, such as decoction of alum and fennel and honey in water, and the like
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then put the patient on his back, put on gloves of linen of the same size, not too tight or too loose, then put the thumb of the hand on the cushion, and hold the shoulder firmly, and treat the hand of the patient
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and another minister holds the chief of the patient, so that it does not move backwards;
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	That shoulder is back now, and if you see that it has been reset thus far,
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	It has returned to its place now, and if you see that it has been reset like this so far, and that you make it stay present in this home which is greater than the patient;
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	then let the patient rest for a while beside the cost, and let the shoulder hang down from the patient’s side, and keep the patient’s head up, so that the patient hangs there like that.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and another attendant treats the patient’s hand behind the belly
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is regained, in whatever way, if you put a ball of wool of equal size under the armpit, then put the plaster on the abscess with powdered oatmeal, with incense and egg-white, on the whole shoulder and around, and strain the armpit outwards again, and bind the limb over the plaster, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And the reset is done in another way too.
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is done by grasping the limb with a long cushion in the earth, from which the head of the shoulder is just as round as a ball, and is neither too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	Then let the patient lie down, but that he have a cloth of wool above, and that the patient be at rest for a long time.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then extend his arm upwards from the other side, and the joint will return to its place immediately
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not return by these means that we have said, if you do this cure:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take two thumbs and three fingers wide, which have the head bent inwards so that it enters through the hole of the armpit, like this
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then hold on the head of the arm the wool cloth that is above, so that it does not bleed the patient, and then put it over the armpit of the patient
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extend your arms upwards towards the chest, and hold the assistant on the arm, and the hand at the head of the arm, then put the arm on one inch of a handbreadth, and hold the thumbs and index finger downwards, and leave the rest hanging downwards:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The jointure returns now.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it does not heal after twenty-five days, and the limb cannot be lifted, then know that the nerves of the shoulder are crushed or stretched or softened; and that the joint will never be fixed in its place again
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he move gently, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal better thus;
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move again after five or seven days, and move it
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if it is stiff and is not softened, it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And when the healing has passed, if there is stiffness in the limb and late mobility, if the patient uses the limb many times, as long as the stiffness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it comes loose after seven days, and the jointure does not stay in place, and cannot lift his upper arm, then the nerves of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened.</start_of_turn>
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and the jointure never stays fixed in its place.</start_of_turn
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation which is towards the elbow, and the upper arm, or behind, if it is done by impulse, and extension of the hands, and is administered with another bandage;
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and heals as soon as it is set right.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the patient with the oil, if he can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked, and cannot hold the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	The swelling of the joint becomes loosened by blows, and again returns;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and has become loosened throughout, both front and back, and the dislocation does not recover, for it is seen and felt well
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	because of excessive deformity
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it can be restored, when it is like this that you can bring it back, you must extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down toward your belly according to the patient’s situation, front and back, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, if it returns when the hand doubles over its hand, and the thumb is firm at the root that is deshydrated.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	Therefore you must immediately reset it even if you must do it several times, for if you leave it alone it will worsen
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And by chance it cannot be brought back whole, even when it is at the back.

Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	If it is restored when it is like this, that you can bring it back, then you stretch out your hand with both hands.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the arms are spread out, and the hands down towards the belly as much as the pain will allow, from the outside and from the inside, and join the joint together with its pieces joined, or at the root of its bone, until it returns to its place
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint is reset, and it moves, bathe and rub well, and press until it is eased; or place upon the joint a fatty mutton nail, then leave it in for a night, and the bone, and wash; and when it sweats, gently wipe the joint, then put the nail back, and then wash again; do this twice or thrice until it is healed. If you see that it returns to its place, put upon it moist butter warmed with burr, and strain it; if it returns to its place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, give great extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	And two assistants must extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during extension;
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	Then twist the arm from the shoulder downwards, and when you have enveloped a double-length and wide bandage around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you look at the joint at its joint, if the bone has any oil on it to smooth the joint, then hold the joint steady until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in its place, put on a dry plaster with egg albumin, and hold the arm to the patient’s chest, and leave it there for some days, and then remove it.</start_of_turn>

puis le deslie.	Then he lets go.

Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I will look and put his hand on that appearance of the joint.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The shoulder joint has been dislocated and the return is easy, more than the others.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to reduce it immediately while it is still dislocated, even if the limb is swollen or if there is bleeding at the site
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And you must place the affected limb on a table and extend the limb, and look that it is even, so that he places his palm on the surface of the joint and holds it until it returns to its place
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, you must watch if it is well back in place;
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Then put the patient’s hand behind his back on the table at extension and reduction.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the limb is in its place, if you place the displacement that we have mentioned, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove and leave it in peace.</start_of_turn
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it comes back now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the strain of the supporting cushions has calmed after the incision, and you let it rest in its natural position, it will recover
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot bear it, and you do not put it back in its place after a few days, the joint will become stiff
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	neither does it harm the patient except as long as the limb is limp, and it cannot withstand any tension at all.

Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the thumb detached from the wrist at the wrist-bone or at the palm or belly; therefore must the thumb stay fixed, and hold the dislocation back in their pouches until it returns, then support the head of the thumb, and guide it to the part where it is joined; and leave it for two days, and then put it back in its place; and do not touch it, as we have said, and withdraw from it, and make it move, and bind it; do this often, until it is straitened, and do the same if it is detached at the belly of the thumb, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is detached from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	and do the same if it is loosened from the shoulder.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no remedy, for the patient’s life is in danger.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never are the thumbs discharged from the wrist part, never at the back of the palm or in the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then they are loosened, and the dislocation must be reduced from your armpits until it returns; then support the head of the thumb, and bring it towards the part where it is joined.

et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And in the same way, do this when it is loosened from another side.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, they say that the old methods of treatment were with great words, which did not yield much; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes before the heel, there is no healing; and that which comes directly on both sides, we cannot cure it except for that which comes from behind; as I have said; and that the patient’s face should be stretched out one inch wide, and should be strained from his knees up; then I take a fist and put it under the heel, and I put another hand over the toes, and I tie a thread around the patient’s ankle, and I take another hand and I take hold of the shin, and I tie two threads between the two toes; and let them be well closed, as I have said, and the patient should keep his palms on the spine until it returns.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And if the symptoms seem to be reversed, that is, if the swelling moves towards the joints, it cannot be held, and often makes the limb limp, or the two thighs or two arms or one leg limp.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	Many times it moves to three parts;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	The part which moves at the back is called "gilbositez":
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The cure is that if the dislocation comes from childhood
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	if there is no cure or healing of all
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	The one which comes from leaning or blows or similar things, they say is an old way of curing by great words, or there is no benefit at all in them.

Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes before the bite, there is no health to be found;

et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And that the patient be extended on his face in one league equal, and have strain from his eyes, that he does not move.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then I take hold of the fist at the shoulder in the earth form, and another has a piece, and I bind the linen around the belly of the patient, and another has haunches, and has knees, and has ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	And two ministers know the bonds, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two thumbs;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And be well closed, the thumb as we have said, and the eye looks puts its palms on the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this treatment, take a thumb three fingers long, and support the base with your hand, and let the patient lie on their side, and hold the thumb base with your hand, and put the middle of the thumb on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and put the eye their thumbs on the other head of the thumb, and press well, until it returns to its place
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if you see that it is turning at the wrist, do the loop that turns the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you hold two fingers at the head of the patient’s arm of great length, and on the piece two others, and between each finger, a suture and a dressing, a palm of space of length.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and between each finger there is one hole, or the knot is corrected, and the fingers are firmly fixed in the ground, so that they do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between the two fingers there is one turning, so that the limb turns, and there are two small fingers of a palm’s length at the turning; for the knot to hold
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	then the ligament which is among the armpits to the turning at the head, and the other ligament to the pieces at the other turning, and the fingers of the attendants turn their turning all along the limb, and the master puts the pin even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are even, put upon a dry patch with an abundance of oil, and then press, and then support with a tablet of three fingers’ length, that the redness of the swelling and the painful part of the ribcage, then bind with a thread, as we have said, and use the patient some nourishment secretly until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	And if nothing comes to an end of the sickness, if you must administer soothing and calming medicines, with the support that we have said before
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	And never give a dose of poison, and never does the appearance of a swelling on the lower back or the loin indicate anything other than dislocation

Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of this is that if this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	The joints of the hip and shoulder only come loose from dislocation, never from other parts;
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	The hip joint is loosened in three parts:
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	frontally and backwards, and frontally and backwards.
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The more forward it is, the more it is loosened in front and behind
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	When the limb is joined with the limb at the dislocation, if it is longer, and if the patient’s knee is greater than the thigh, it cannot bend his knee even with fire
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	This is because the head of the humerus is dislocated from the socket, which is why the shoulder joint comes loose
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	If this semblance of dislocation persists, if it is an old dislocation, and it remains as it is without any cure; and one must not presume otherwise.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the sign of the one who has it in front, if he has his limb well according to its completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And thus, do not double the knee joint in pain, and if you see him do so, do not allow it before, and retain his urine, and swell his belly, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, it is necessary to apply a strong minister, and keep the limb firm with two hands, or one, as you please; and another minister stretches out his hand above in part as much as he can stretch out his hands below his buttocks, then he grasps it with a loop of thread above the knee; and another holds the head of the limb; and they stretch up and down together until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains so
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	Return the patient to this semblance of dislocation if indeed the dislocation is old and persists according to its nature, if there is no remedy for it;
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and do not presume it
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And in this case where the dislocation is fresh, and there are three ways of dislocation, if you hurry that you turn the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it forward and backward;
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	By chance if it returns, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	If it does not return in this manner, if you must force it, grasp it firmly with two hands, or with one hand that you must bind on the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and another helper extends his hand under in part as much as he can stretch out his hands below his buttocks, and then grasp it with a loop of thread on the hip
