et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and extend upwards and downwards at the same time, until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains so hanging
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation is pushed out, if the patient lies still as we have said in the case of Gilbert, grasp the limb firmly with one hand and the heel with the other; then insert two fingers, one at the wrist and the other at the ankle, and press one finger between the thighs of the patient in the shape of a triangle; and plant damp cloths around, so that it does not bleed excessively, then extend the thumbs ministering to him, and the master looks at the patient’s hand to set the dislocation.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this does not work, it is necessary to make an incision to his appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When the dislocation is in the shoulder, if you can, soothe the patient over his costal cartilage, then place the limb on the root of the humerus, and the bone which is beside the scapula, and extend the limb upwards towards the scapula and towards the acromion.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then grasp another assistant by the arms, and embrace the great bone of the painful arm, and extend it towards the front:
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of dislocation is less severe than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you do not manage to fix it in this way that we have said, if you can, bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread above the two toes, and above the two knees, and let the painful limb be extended twice as much as the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	Then either hang it above the head of a staff, or on two arms of length.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then command the minister to grasp the head of the limb, and let another minister hang alongside the patient, who graspes the limb firmly, because the joint is now returning steadily.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is loosened, if the patient is conscious, as we have said concerning embolism, grasp the limb properly above and below the painful area.</start_of_turn
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then put two cushions, one at the head and one at the foot, and insert one cushion between the limbs of the patient in the form of an X.</start_of_turn
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And place moist towels around it, so that it does not bruise the patient, and extend the thumbs of the ministers towards him, and the patient places his hand on the dislocation.</start_of_turn
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is pushed out, if it does not manage to extend the limb downwards, do not lift it up from the ground, but know that it must be as it was before the dislocation; as we have said concerning the two inches; and that it must be supported on its face, and the limb must be stretched as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and it will be finished when the patient extends his leg, and they will be equal; then join the thighs and put on the dressing, and bind with a bandage, so that the limb does not move; and let it rest for three days or four, then take it off and put on the dressing again; and if you see that they are equal, if the bandage is as before, and leave it for three days; then take it off and make the limb relaxed, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	And thus rests for two or three days, then releases and places the support over it; and if you see that they are even, if strained, as before, leave it for two days; then releases and make him blink attentively, until the limb is comforted.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is forward, if you must, extend the affected limb strongly, as I have said.
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the eye of pain on the painful side, then press with the other hand, and extend the limb backwards towards the armpit.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is backwards, if you cannot extend the limb backwards, do not lift it from the ground, but rather keep it as it was dislocated backwards, as we have said above about the two fingers;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	or be on its face, and the limb is stretched as we have said above, and must press on the joint at the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be known when the patient extends his limb, and they will be even;
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	Therefore join the thighs, and put the cushion in place, and strain a bandage tightly, so that the limb does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three days or four, then remove it, and put the cushion back on
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see that they are even, if the strain is as before, and leave for three days
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then remove it, and let him breathe easily, until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not displaced, if an extension is administered strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The shoulder joint is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	namely, forward and backward, and downward;
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not damage the front part.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you order the patient to bend his limb towards his thigh, and if he does not feel it towards his thigh, his muscles are dislocated;
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And restore all of them if you make the patient sit upright, and extend his limb if he can, and place your hand on his face, and put his thumb on your knees.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take his shoulder joint at your palms, and pull between your thumbs, and fold the two ribs of his shoulder joint together
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And another attendant extends his thumb, until the shoulder joint returns to its place, and the sign is that his limb is properly aligned with his thigh slightly bent
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	Put on the dressing and make the limb swell at the thigh, and keep it bound for three days or four, and then take it off
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And do not move the patient any more, until the limb is comfortable.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is if the ankle is loosened, and try before towards the part where it is loosened: bring it back if it is slight, and extend it slightly with your hands when it is slightly stretched only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is thoroughly dry, if you think you have set the limb straight, hold the patient firmly by the leg above the ankle; then pull the limb towards you with your right hand, then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and hold it firmly; do this twice as we have said, slowly pulling and stretching; if it returns, that is well; if not, repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return, make the patient lie face down on the ground, and fix his heel firmly on the ground between his thighs, and put a bandage around it, so that it does not bleed the patient; then hold the patient’s thigh, and another helper extend the limb with your hands or at the wrist, which is on the ankle; then extend the ankles of the helpers equally, and hold the limb firmly either between the patient’s thighs to keep the patient steady when extending it; then put the eyes equally on the dislocation with your hands, and another helper holds the limb steady at the ankle, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it comes to a boil, if you put on the dressing and stamp on it, and the swelling forms, and you bind the limb to the leg, and keep the nerves which are above the ankle behind, so that they are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the swelling subsides, if the strain is gone; then remove the dressing in a third or fourth part, and warn the patient for three days; and if he goes before this limit, it is not certain that he will not damage himself further.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and that it swells up before at the part where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	If the swelling is slight, it must be gently extended with the hands when it is only slightly swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is thoroughly dried out, it must be made to sit upright; and hold the patient firmly by the limb under the ankle
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the thumb to your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, and then stretch upwards, and keep the limb well stretched out
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice, as we have said, with the heel bent and the limb pulled out
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	if it returns, it is well done
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	If not, if you begin again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	If it cannot return, if you make the patient lie face down on the ground, and press his heel firmly to the ground between his thighs, and tie a cloth around his waist, that he does not move the patient; and let him rest.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then hold the limb at the elbow, and another assistant extends the limb at the wrist or at the shoulder, that it lies on the collarbone of the limb; and let him rest
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend the thumbs of the assistants evenly, and pass the pack either inside between the thighs of the patient to hold the patient when he is extended; and let him rest.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then put the eyes equally on the dislocation with his hands, and another assistant grasps the limb at the shoulder, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it [the dislocation] is at a point, if you place the padding and bind above, and the strain forms, and you tie the limb to the leg, and guard the nerves that are above the ankle behind, that the ligature is not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then leave it for two or three days, and if the strain relaxes, if the tension;
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then loosen it after a third or a fourth, and tell the patient to sleep for three days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he goes before this time, it is not certain that he will not be deformed forever.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is not in any knot of the limb, then you must make the patient sit on one leg or on the ground quite straight, and put your limb on what is open of these joints, and press your limb firmly until it returns; and when it is even, and there is no opening, if you put on the dressing of the limb two fingers, then the strain forms, and leave it for three days, then remove it; and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	When there is wound and dislocation together,
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times the patient dies: if you are not mindful of me and do not know how to cure it, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and timely, do not be bold; and begin with gentle treatments to the wound, and leave the patient in the hands of the Lord, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you restore the limb to its place, even if the wound has burst; and when the limb is restored, if you administer gentle treatments to the wound, and cure the wound, as it should be, from dried pus; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are broken, if the bones are fractured, do as we have said in simple illnesses; and you must abstain from pride, as I have said, for this is harmful to you according to your Creator, and for the salvation of your soul and body.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is not in any place of the limb, if you must make the patient sit on one knee or on a bench quite upright, and put your limb on what is open of these joints, then press your limb until it returns
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when they are even, and nothing is open, if you put two ounces of rue marigold on a table at two joints, then the pain will grow, and you must leave it for three days, and then remove it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and rest it until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When wound is associated with dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times it happens that the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not modest in the treatment, and if you do not understand the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and timely, do not be rash;
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and use soothing things first and afterwards, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, if you first reset the limb in its place, as the apostemes were before;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, if you administer soothing things afterwards, and treat the wound, as it seems appropriate, with desiccant ointments
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and the bones are broken, if the bones themselves, do as we have said in simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	And take care not to enter into fear, as I have said, for this will bring you misery according to your Creator, and for the safety of your arm and body.
